Uses the VS Code extension \u2014 means Claude Code can drive Playwright with cursor-style commands.\n- **Official Playwright YouTube channel** (https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC46Zj8pDH5tDosqm1gd7WTg) \u2014 has a **Playwright MCP** playlist (very relevant \u2014 lets Claude Code drive a browser directly).\n- **Software Testing with Playwright** \u2014 freeCodeCamp (~1 hr) \u2014 explains *why* before *how*.\n- **Playwright Tutorial Crash Course using TypeScript** \u2014 Dilpreet Johal \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ov9e_F8I5zc.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f No \"Playwright in 100 Seconds\" by Fireship exists.\n\n### Docker (conceptual only)\n\n**Written:**\n- **Docker Docs \u2014 What is a container?** (https://www.docker.com/resources/what-container/) \u2014 5 min, pure concept.\n- **Docker Get started overview** (https://docs.docker.com/get-started/overview/) \u2014 containers vs VMs, images, registries.\n\n**YouTube \u2014 keep it to the first two:**\n- **Docker in 100 Seconds** \u2014 Fireship \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Gjnup-PuquQ (1:40). **Start here.** Fastest visual \"what & why\" on the internet.\n- **You need to learn Docker RIGHT NOW!! // Docker Containers 101** \u2014 NetworkChuck (https://networkchuck.com/you-need-to-learn-docker-right-now-docker-containers-101/, ~25 min). Compares VMs \u2192 Docker visually; perfect conceptual level.\n- **Learn Docker in 7 Easy Steps** \u2014 Fireship (~10 min). Slightly deeper but still concept-first.\n- *Optional:* **Docker Tutorial for Beginners** \u2014 TechWorld with Nana (https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLy7NrYWoggjzfAHlUusx2wuDwfCrmJYcs) \u2014 only watch first 30 min (Intro \u2192 Docker vs VM \u2192 Main Commands).\n\n### Claude API / LLM APIs / prompt engineering\n\n**Written/interactive:**\n- **Anthropic Prompt Engineering Interactive Tutorial** (https://github.com/anthropics/prompt-eng-interactive-tutorial) \u2014 9 chapters + appendix. **Google Sheets version requires zero code setup** \u2014 ideal for Daniel.\n- **Anthropic Academy** (https://anthropic.skilljar.com/) \u2014 free, official certs. Daniel should take: **Claude 101**, **Claude with the Anthropic API**, **Claude Code 101**, **Prompt Engineering Interactive Tutorial**.\n- **Anthropic Docs \u2014 Prompt engineering overview** (https://docs.anthropic.com/en/docs/build-with-claude/prompt-engineering/overview).\n- **DeepLearning.AI \u2014 ChatGPT Prompt Engineering for Developers (Ng + Fulford)** (https://learn.deeplearning.ai/courses/chatgpt-prompt-eng/) \u2014 ~1 hr, free, browser Jupyter notebooks. Principles transfer 1:1 to Claude.\n\n**YouTube:**\n- **ChatGPT Prompt Engineering for Developers Free Course** \u2014 full Ng/Fulford upload \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tRvcAdqsJWo.\n- **Anthropic's own YouTube channel** \u2014 \"Prompting 101,\" \"Claude Code in Action,\" researcher explainers (5\u201315 min each).\n\n### Vercel AI SDK\n\n**Written/interactive:**\n- **Vercel AI SDK Docs \u2014 Foundations + Getting Started** (https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/foundations, https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started) \u2014 ~30 min. Concept-organized.\n- **Vercel AI SDK Overview** (https://vercel.com/docs/ai-sdk) \u2014 crisply explains *why* the SDK exists.\n- **Matt Pocock's Vercel AI SDK Tutorial (AI Hero, FREE)** (https://www.aihero.dev/vercel-ai-sdk-tutorial) \u2014 **16 lessons, completely free**, written + video hybrid. Best single resource on this list.\n- **AI SDK v6 Crash Course GitHub** (https://github.com/ai-hero-dev/ai-sdk-v6-crash-course) \u2014 57 exercises Claude Code can mostly do for him.\n- **Vercel AI Gateway** (https://vercel.com/docs/ai-gateway/getting-started) \u2014 one API key \u2192 100+ models.\n\n**YouTube:**\n- **AI SDK v5: A Crash Course | Matt Pocock at React Universe Conf 2025** \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ihHLs6v7Lko (~30\u201340 min). Pocock teaches \"from the outside in\" \u2014 exactly Daniel's mindset.\n- **A Complete Guide To Vercel's AI SDK** \u2014 Matt Pocock \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mojZpktAiYQ.\n- **Vercel AI SDK in React (Beginner Tutorial)** \u2014 Cosden Solutions \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y4IMq43KvRw.\n- **Build a Support Agent with Vercel AI SDK \u2013 Full Tutorial** \u2014 freeCodeCamp \u2014 https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WKIjkxxNH0c.\n\n### Whisper / speech-to-text\n\n**Written:**\n- **OpenAI Whisper announcement** (https://openai.com/index/whisper/) \u2014 10 min. The canonical \"why Whisper exists.\"\n- **How Whisper AI Works (OpenWhispr)** (https://openwhispr.com/blog/how-whisper-ai-works) \u2014 well-illustrated, plain-English.\n- **AssemblyAI: OpenAI Whisper for developers** (https://www.assemblyai.com/blog/openai-whisper-developers-choosing-api-local-server-side-transcription) \u2014 three deployment options compared.\n- **faster-whisper README** (https://github.com/SYSTRAN/faster-whisper).\n- **WhisperX README** (https://github.com/m-bain/whisperX) \u2014 adds word timestamps + diarization.\n- **WhisperKit** (https://github.com/argmaxinc/WhisperKit) \u2014 on-device Mac/iPhone.\n\n**YouTube:**\n- **OpenAI's Whisper Model Explained** \u2014 Louis Bouchard (What's AI) \u2014 companion blog https://www.louisbouchard.ai/whisper/ (~6 min). Visual diagrams without math.\n- **AssemblyAI channel** (https://www.youtube.com/@AssemblyAI) \u2014 multiple short Whisper explainers, 5\u201315 min each.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f No Fireship \"Whisper in 100 Seconds.\" Use Bouchard's video instead.\n\n**Conceptual frame for Daniel:** Three Whisper flavors matter: (a) **OpenAI Whisper API** \u2014 pay-per-minute hosted; (b) **faster-whisper / WhisperX** \u2014 local GPU, free, private, word-level timestamps + diarization (best for interview transcripts); (c) **WhisperKit** \u2014 on-device Apple Silicon.\n\n---\n\n## Part 2 \u2014 \"Why this tool over alternatives\"\n\n### JavaScript/TypeScript vs Python for automation/glue code\n\n**Why JS/TS wins:** Daniel's system is overwhelmingly I/O-bound \u2014 wait for API, do next thing. Node.js was designed around exactly that pattern; its event loop handles hundreds of concurrent API calls without breaking a sweat (benchmarks at https://dev.to/m-a-h-b-u-b/nodejs-vs-python-real-benchmarks-performance-insights-and-scalability-analysis-4dm5 show ~44% higher requests/sec than Python FastAPI on I/O loads). Cloud vendors ship JS SDKs first because so many devs use Node \u2014 `dropbox-sdk-js`, `googleapis`, `@vercel/ai`, `basic-ftp`, `playwright`, `youtubeuploader` wrappers all live on npm. npm has 2M+ packages, biggest ecosystem on Earth. Native `async/await` reads top-to-bottom like a script. One language top-to-bottom if he ever builds a dashboard.\n\n**When Python is better:** Anything ML/data \u2014 Whisper, PyTorch, NumPy, ffmpeg pipelines. (See section 3.) Also the simplest scripting syntax for short scripts.\n\n**TV-producer analogy:** JavaScript = a walkie-talkie \u2014 designed to juggle many short conversations. Python = an editor's workstation \u2014 slower at juggling, unbeatable for heavy lifts.\n\n### TypeScript over plain JavaScript\n\nJS will silently let you pass a string where a number was expected; you find out when it crashes at 2am during an upload. TypeScript catches it at edit time. Massively better IDE autocomplete. Refactor-safety: rename a field, TS shows every break. **The killer reason for Daniel: AI coding tools work dramatically better with TS.** The GitHub Octoverse 2025 report found ~94% of LLM-generated code compilation errors are type-related \u2014 TypeScript catches those at compile time (see https://www.builder.io/blog/typescript-vs-javascript, https://thomaslandgraf.substack.com/p/why-i-choose-typescript-for-llmbased). Types act as a spec the LLM reads, so Claude generates more accurate, less hallucinated code.\n\n**When plain JS is fine:** One-off throwaway scripts, tiny prototypes, when learning JS itself.\n\n**Analogy:** Plain JS = shooting without script supervision \u2014 fast and free until continuity breaks. TS = a script supervisor flagging every line that doesn't match earlier setups.\n\n### Python for ML / Whisper\n\nThe entire ML research world standardized on Python in the late 2000s. PyTorch, TensorFlow, JAX, Hugging Face Transformers, scikit-learn, NumPy \u2014 all Python-first. Python is slow, but NumPy/PyTorch/CTranslate2 are thin Python wrappers around fast C/C++/CUDA code (the \"glue language\" pattern; PyTorch paper https://arxiv.org/pdf/1912.01703). New models drop on Hugging Face in Python first. faster-whisper wraps CTranslate2 (C++ inference engine) and WhisperX uses pyannote.audio (Python-only) for diarization \u2014 that's why both are Python.\n\n**When JS/something else wins:** Browser transcription (transformers.js, whisper.cpp WASM), embedded/edge devices, one-shot CLI use where you can shell out.\n\n**Analogy:** Python = the post house everyone in town uses. You *could* grade your show elsewhere, but every colorist, plugin, and LUT was built for that one shop.\n\n### n8n vs Zapier vs Make.com vs raw scripts vs Airflow\n\n| | Model | Cost | Ceiling |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **Zapier** | Cloud no-code | Per task (every step) | Low complexity, 7,000+ apps |\n| **Make.com** | Cloud visual | Per operation | Medium |\n| **n8n** | Self-hostable fair-code | Per execution; self-host free | Very high |\n| **Raw scripts** | TS/Python + cron | Free | Unlimited, you build everything |\n| **Airflow** | Python DAGs | Self-host | Industrial pipelines |\n\n**Why n8n wins for Daniel:** Self-hosted = data ownership (matters for client material). Code escape hatch \u2014 every node can run custom JavaScript, so Claude/Cursor can write n8n code nodes for you. Cost: Zapier counts every step (10-step workflow \u00d7 1,000 runs = 10,000 tasks); n8n self-hosted = $0 incremental (https://www.buildberg.co/blog/n8n-vs-make-vs-zapier). Per-execution billing on n8n Cloud is more predictable. First-class AI/LangChain nodes.\n\n**When alternatives win:** Zapier for zero-setup non-technical solo users with broad app catalog. Make for visual users outgrowing Zapier but not self-hosting. Raw scripts when workflow is simple and you want it in version control. Airflow for big teams with thousands of DAGs.\n\n**n8n downside:** Real learning curve. The Zapier blog itself admits n8n \"expects you to know what you're doing\" (https://zapier.com/blog/n8n-vs-make/).\n\n**Analogy:** Zapier = press-button effects switcher. Make = full vision mixer with patch bay. n8n = your own edit suite where you can rewire anything but you maintain it.\n\n### Playwright vs Selenium vs Puppeteer vs Cypress\n\n**Why Playwright wins:** Auto-wait built in \u2014 automatically waits for elements before clicking, killing Selenium's flakiness (the feature that converts ex-Selenium users). One API across Chromium, Firefox, WebKit (Safari). Puppeteer is Chromium-only; Cypress is essentially Chromium. The core Playwright engineers came from the Puppeteer team at Google and rebuilt at Microsoft with multi-browser support. Checkly's benchmark puts Playwright ~23% faster than Cypress and Selenium for long suites (https://www.checklyhq.com/blog/cypress-vs-selenium-vs-playwright-vs-puppeteer-speed-comparison/). Trace viewer + codegen \u2014 record actions in the browser and it writes the code. First-class headless support (critical on a Linux media server). TypeScript-native.\n\n**When alternatives win:** Selenium for legacy IE/old Edge or multi-language enterprise teams. Cypress for single-app frontend DX with time-travel debugging. Puppeteer for Chrome-only simple scraping.\n\n**Analogy:** Selenium = a 2004 studio camera \u2014 works everywhere, heavy, fiddly to focus. Playwright = a modern mirrorless: lighter, faster, autofocus that nails it, any \"format.\"\n\n### faster-whisper / WhisperX over vanilla Whisper\n\n**The lineage:** OpenAI Whisper (2022, PyTorch) \u2192 faster-whisper (SYSTRAN) swaps inference engine to **CTranslate2** (C++) with quantization \u2192 WhisperX (Max Bain, Oxford) uses faster-whisper internally and adds **forced alignment** (wav2vec2 word-level timestamps) + **speaker diarization** (pyannote.audio).\n\n**faster-whisper:** \"Up to 4\u00d7 faster than openai/whisper for the same accuracy while using less memory\" (official README https://github.com/SYSTRAN/faster-whisper). INT8 quantization lets large-v3 run on modest GPU or CPU. Batched faster-whisper hits ~12.5\u00d7 speedup on long files (https://mobiusml.github.io/batched_whisper_blog/).\n\n**WhisperX:** Word-level timestamps \u2014 critical for SRT/VTT captions. Speaker diarization \u2014 essential for multi-host shows, interviews, panels. Same transcription speed as faster-whisper plus small alignment overhead.\n\n**Tradeoffs:** faster-whisper has CUDA/cuDNN version pickiness (https://modal.com/blog/choosing-whisper-variants). WhisperX requires pyannote license + Hugging Face token.\n\n**Analogy:** Vanilla Whisper = master tape. faster-whisper = faster, smaller dub same quality. WhisperX = the dub *with* timecode burn-in and speaker labels baked in.\n\n### Vercel AI SDK vs direct Claude SDK\n\n**Why Vercel AI SDK:** One-line provider swap \u2014 change `'anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'` to `'openai/gpt-5'` and code keeps working. Hedge against outages and price changes. `generateObject` with Zod schema returns validated typed JSON across providers. Tool calling abstraction handles provider-specific JSON schema gymnastics. React hooks (`useChat`, `useCompletion`) for streaming chat UI in ~10 lines. Streaming standardized across providers (Strapi reports ~60% boilerplate reduction https://strapi.io/blog/openai-sdk-vs-vercel-ai-sdk-comparison). Full TypeScript types. MCP support.\n\n**When direct Anthropic SDK wins:** **Prompt caching** \u2014 Anthropic's `cache_control` (the biggest cost saver for large repeated system prompts) is fully exposed only via the direct SDK as of writing (https://www.pkgpulse.com/guides/vercel-ai-sdk-vs-openai-sdk-vs-anthropic-sdk-2026). Day-one access to new Anthropic features (extended thinking, computer use). Provider-specific Batch/Files APIs. Slight latency penalty on Gateway (~15% on small prompts) https://dev.to/cliftonz/benchmarking-vercel-ai-gateway-against-the-native-anthropic-sdk-21g5.\n\n**Analogy:** Vercel AI SDK = universal lens-mount adapter \u2014 any \"brand\" of model fits the same body. Direct Anthropic SDK = native mount: tightest fit, every feature exposed, locked to that brand.\n\n### SQLite vs hosted DB vs Notion\n\n**SQLite is the right call for a single-user automation system.** It's a single file you can back up, copy, email. Zero configuration. From the SQLite team itself: *\"SQLite does not compete with client/server databases. SQLite competes with `fopen()`\"* (https://sqlite.org/whentouse.html). In-process = sub-millisecond reads, often faster than Postgres for a single-server app (https://www.epicweb.dev/why-you-should-probably-be-using-sqlite). Production-grade \u2014 in every iPhone, Android, Chrome, Firefox. Trillions of deployments. Handles concurrent reads + one writer well under WAL mode.\n\n**Postgres/MySQL when:** Multiple machines writing simultaneously (SQLite allows only one writer). Heavy write concurrency. You want a hosted, replicated, backed-up service.\n\n**Notion as a \"DB\":** Great as a human-facing UI. Useless as a real DB \u2014 rate-limited (~3 req/sec per integration), no joins/transactions/constraints, slow (hundreds of ms per call), no schema enforcement, eventual consistency.\n\n**Recommended pattern for Daniel:** SQLite = source of truth. Notion = read-only mirror pushed to from SQLite. Best of both.\n\n**Analogy:** SQLite = local production binder always with you. Postgres = shared production-office filing system. Notion = pretty whiteboard in the conference room \u2014 great for humans, terrible to compute against.\n\n### Docker \u2014 what it solves, why NOT on production\n\n**Problem solved:** \"Works on my machine.\" Containers package an app + dependencies + runtime into an image that runs identically anywhere. **Containers vs VMs:** VMs boot a full guest OS on a hypervisor \u2014 gigabytes RAM, minutes to start. Containers share the host kernel and package only userspace \u2014 megabytes, sub-second startup.\n\n**Why his advisors say NOT to run it on the production media server (solo operator):**\n1. **GPU passthrough is painful** \u2014 Nvidia containers need the NVIDIA Container Toolkit + driver match; Intel QuickSync needs `/dev/dri` mapping + `render` group permissions. Every driver update can break passthrough. Native install = GPU just works (https://forum.proxmox.com/threads/gpu-passthrough-to-container-lxc.132518/).\n2. **File-permission headaches** \u2014 container UIDs rarely match host UIDs owning media drives; files end up owned by `root:root` or random UID; `PUID`/`PGID` works but is fiddly and constantly breaks.\n3. **Overhead for a solo operator** \u2014 daemon to maintain, networking bridges, port mappings, volume management, image-storage bloat, separate log location. For one person, `pm2` or `systemd` native services are simpler.\n4. **Performance** \u2014 media transcoding and ML inference want direct hardware access.\n5. **Debugging is harder** \u2014 every peek requires `docker exec`.\n\n**When Docker IS the right call for him:** n8n itself (officially recommended as Docker), services he wants to start/stop cleanly (a Postgres or Redis), any future cloud/k8s deployment.\n\n**Analogy:** Docker = shipping a movie as a DCP \u2014 whole package locked together so any cinema plays identically. Great for distribution. But in your own edit suite where you own the gear, you don't need DCP.\n\n### FTPS vs SFTP vs FTP\n\n| | What | Port | Encryption |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **FTP** | Original 1971 protocol | 21 + dynamic | None |\n| **FTPS** | FTP wrapped in TLS | 21 or 990 + dynamic | TLS (like HTTPS) |\n| **SFTP** | SSH file transfer subsystem \u2014 *not actually FTP* | 22 only | SSH (whole session) |\n\n**Critical clarification:** FTPS = old FTP + TLS handshake (like HTTP \u2192 HTTPS). SFTP = a completely different protocol that rides on SSH and just happens to also transfer files. They're not variants of each other.\n\n**Why a CDN like StreamHoster requires FTPS specifically:** Many CDNs standardized on FTPS because their backend storage (proprietary FTP servers, IIS) supports it natively, and they want to keep the FTP command structure their customers' clients already speak. SFTP requires an SSH server \u2014 a much bigger attack surface. So FTPS lets them encrypt without changing protocol semantics. If your CDN says \"FTPS,\" use FTPS. The `basic-ftp` Node library supports both FTP and FTPS via `secure: true`.\n\n**Plain FTP:** Passwords and contents visible to anyone sniffing. **Never over the internet.**\n\n**Sources:** https://www.exavault.com/blog/difference-between-ftp-ftps-and-sftp, https://www.cerberusftp.com/blog/ftps-vs-sftp-understanding-the-difference/.\n\n**Analogy:** FTP = manila envelope unsealed in interoffice mail. FTPS = same envelope in a tamper-evident security pouch. SFTP = a completely different courier service (SSH) that happens to also carry envelopes.\n\n### OAuth vs API keys vs passwords\n\n**Username + password:** Your script logs in as the user. **Never.** Full account control if leaked; breaks the moment user enables 2FA.\n\n**API key:** A long random string identifying *your application*. Best for server-to-server with no user concept (your own OpenAI/Anthropic key).\n\n**OAuth 2.0:** User logs in *with the provider* (Google/YouTube), grants your app limited permissions called **scopes**, provider issues a short-lived **access token** + long-lived **refresh token**. Your app never sees the user's password (https://oauth.net/2/).\n\n**Why YouTube Data API uses OAuth:** Scopes (request only `youtube.upload`, not full account). Revocable from user's Google account page without password change. 2FA-compatible. Auditable \u2014 provider knows which app did what. Refresh tokens let scripts run for months without re-login.\n\n**The famous \"valet key\" analogy** (from Nate Barbettini's must-watch talk https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=996OiexHze0): *A valet key starts the car and locks/unlocks it but won't open the trunk or glove compartment, and limits top speed. You give the valet a limited capability \u2014 not your full key.*\n\n**When API keys are correct:** Server-to-server with no human user (Anthropic, OpenAI, CDN upload). Your own account, no delegation.\n\n**Analogy:** Password = your house keys + alarm code. API key = a code that opens the back door, all rooms, until you change it. OAuth = a smart lock that says \"let the cleaner in Tuesdays 10\u201312 to the kitchen only, and the cleaner can't make copies.\"\n\n### Credential vault (1Password CLI) vs `.env` vs hardcoding\n\n**Hardcoded in source:** Committed to git history forever; bots scan public repos within seconds. Rotation requires editing and redeploying. #1 cause of GitHub secret leaks.\n\n**`.env` files (12-Factor App, https://12factor.net/config):** Code stays clean; environment-specific files; easy swap. But: plaintext on disk, no audit trail, onboarding pain (email/Slack the `.env`), easy to accidentally commit.\n\n**1Password CLI `op run`:** Store secrets in your vault. `.env` contains references like `ANTHROPIC_KEY=op://Prod/Anthropic/credential`, not real values. At runtime, 1Password fetches the actual secret and injects it as an env var to that one process. **Secrets are never written to disk.** Audit logs. Rotate centrally \u2014 change once in 1Password, every machine gets it next launch. Onboarding = grant vault access. Output masking \u2014 `console.log(API_KEY)` becomes `<concealed by 1Password>` (https://developer.1password.com/docs/cli/secrets-environment-variables/, https://nshipster.com/1password-cli/). `.env` files with only `op://` references are safe to commit.\n\n**When `.env` is enough:** Solo dev, prototype, code never leaves laptop.\n\n**When you need a vault:** Production handling third-party data; multiple machines/services; anything embarrassing to leak.\n\n**Analogy:** Hardcoded = writing the safe combination on the studio wall. `.env` = sticky note in your top drawer. 1Password CLI = combination locked in a real safe, cracked open just long enough to type one number.\n\n### \"When to switch\" cheat sheet\n\n| Tool | Switch to alternative when... |\n|---|---|\n| TS/JS | You need ML/data work \u2192 Python |\n| TypeScript | You're writing a 20-line throwaway script |\n| n8n | 100% non-technical or <100 ops/month \u2192 Zapier |\n| Playwright | Multi-language test team or legacy IE \u2192 Selenium |\n| WhisperX | Only need plain transcription \u2192 faster-whisper |\n| Vercel AI SDK | Need prompt caching / cutting-edge Anthropic features \u2192 direct SDK |\n| SQLite | Multiple machines write simultaneously \u2192 Postgres |\n| Native processes | Cloud deployment or reproducibility \u2192 Docker |\n| SFTP | Vendor requires FTPS \u2192 FTPS |\n| OAuth | Pure server-to-server, no end user \u2192 API key |\n| 1Password vault | Solo dev, throwaway project \u2192 `.env` is fine |\n\n---\n\n## Part 3 \u2014 ADHD-friendly instructional design (research foundation)\n\n### Designing learning for ADHD adults\n\nRussell Barkley's foundational model (Barkley 1997, *Psychological Bulletin*, https://frisch-ot.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/11/EFModelBarkely.pdf) frames ADHD as impaired behavioral inhibition undermining working memory, self-regulation of affect/motivation/arousal, and planning. Barkley's executive-function fact sheet (https://www.russellbarkley.org/factsheets/ADHD_EF_and_SR.pdf) is explicit: **ADHD adults can't reliably self-motivate for tasks lacking immediate salience.**\n\nVolkow et al. (2011), \"Motivation Deficit in ADHD Is Associated with Dysfunction of the Dopamine Reward Pathway,\" *Molecular Psychiatry* (https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC3010326/) used PET imaging to confirm reduced D2/D3 receptor and dopamine-transporter availability in nucleus accumbens \u2014 uninteresting tasks literally fail to recruit the reward system. The authors recommend \"interventions to enhance the saliency of school and work tasks.\"\n\nThis validates William Dodson's clinically popular **INCUP** heuristic \u2014 ADHD attention is reliably engaged by Interest, Novelty, Challenge, Urgency, Passion (https://www.additudemag.com/7-executive-function-deficits-linked-to-adhd/).\n\n**Practical scaffolds with evidence:**\n- **Pomodoro Technique** (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pomodoro_Technique) \u2014 2025 scoping review: \"time-structured Pomodoro interventions consistently improved focus, reduced mental fatigue, and enhanced sustained task performance, outperforming self-paced breaks.\" For ADHD, shorten focus blocks to 10\u201315 min until rhythm establishes (https://lifeskillsadvocate.com/blog/pomodoro-technique-for-adhd/).\n- **Body doubling** (https://chadd.org/adhd-news/adhd-news-adults/adhd-weekly-could-a-body-double-help-you-increase-your-productivity/) \u2014 virtual coworking; CHADD and ADDitude endorse. Mechanism hypothesized: accountability + dopaminergic social cues. Largely anecdotal but consistent.\n- **Jessica McCabe's *How to ADHD*** (https://howtoadhdbook.com/) \u2014 \"boost the signal, reduce the noise,\" \"have less stuff to manage,\" \"build time wisdom\" \u2014 explicit reframings of cognitive-load reduction for ADHD.\n\n### Active recall / retrieval practice (the testing effect)\n\n**Roediger & Karpicke (2006)**, \"Test-Enhanced Learning,\" *Psychological Science* 17(3): 249\u2013255 (https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1111/j.1467-9280.2006.01693.x) is the seminal study. Students who read once + self-tested 3\u00d7 outperformed peers who studied 4\u00d7 on a 1-week delayed test \u2014 even though the studying group felt more confident. **Restudying boosts short-term recall; retrieval boosts durable memory.**\n\n**Robert Bjork's \"desirable difficulties\"** (https://bjorklab.psych.ucla.edu/research/) explains why: effortful retrieval strengthens \"storage strength\" even when \"retrieval strength\" feels low. Bjork & Bjork (2020), JARMAC (https://bjorklab.psych.ucla.edu/wp-content/uploads/sites/13/2021/01/RABjorkELBjorkJARMAC2020ForPostingSingleSpaced.pdf) \u2014 the canonical update.\n\n***Make It Stick*** (Brown, Roediger, McDaniel, 2014, https://www.hup.harvard.edu/catalog.php?isbn=9780674729018) \u2014 eight strategies; most critically: \"learning is deeper and more durable when effortful\" and \"we are poor judges of when we are learning well.\" A K\u201312 implementation cited in the book raised grades from C+ to A\u2212 for an entire year via systematic quizzing.\n\n**Design implications:** Replace re-reading with closed-book recall prompts at the end of every micro-lesson. Free recall first, then multiple-choice. **Pre-tests** prime encoding (Bjork desirable difficulty) \u2014 quiz *before* teaching. Low-stakes, 3\u20135 items per lesson. Immediate feedback after each item potentiates the effect (Roediger & Pyc 2012).\n\n### Spaced repetition\n\nEbbinghaus's 1885 forgetting curve: ~50% of nonsense syllables lost within an hour, ~70% by day's end (https://www.supermemo.com/en/blog/history-of-spaced-repetition). Forgetting is exponential; re-exposure just before forgetting boosts retention dramatically.\n\nPiotr Wo\u017aniak's **SuperMemo SM-2 algorithm** (1987) schedules cards on expanding intervals based on self-rated difficulty \u2014 still the base of Anki. The pre-digital **Leitner system** (1972) does the same with physical card boxes; **Pimsleur** (1967) baked it into audio language lessons.\n\n**Cepeda, Pashler, Vul, Wixted & Rohrer (2006)**, \"Distributed Practice in Verbal Recall,\" *Psychological Bulletin* 132(3): 354\u2013380 (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16719566/; PDF https://augmentingcognition.com/assets/Cepeda2006.pdf) \u2014 meta-analysis of 839 effect sizes across 184 studies. Spaced > massed with medium-to-large effects across ages and content. Cepeda et al. (2008) (https://laplab.ucsd.edu/articles/Cepeda%20et%20al%202008_psychsci.pdf) gives the practical rule: **if you need to remember for X time, space reviews at ~10\u201320% of X.**\n\n**Design implications:** Build a 5-min daily Anki-style flashcard deck for API patterns and syntax. Re-introduce week-1 concepts in weeks 2, 4, 8 \u2014 *interleaved into new lessons*, not standalone \"review modules.\" Expanding intervals (1d \u2192 3d \u2192 7d \u2192 16d) generally outperform fixed. Tolerate forgetting before review.\n\n### Microlearning + optimal lesson length\n\n**Guo, Kim & Rubin (2014)**, \"How Video Production Affects Student Engagement,\" ACM L@S '14 (https://up.csail.mit.edu/other-pubs/las2014-pguo-engagement.pdf) \u2014 6.9M video sessions on edX. **Median engagement maxes at ~6 minutes regardless of video length.** A 9-min and 12-min video both average ~6 min of watch time. Their headline recommendation: \"segment videos into chunks shorter than 6 minutes.\" Bonus findings: informal talking-head > studio lecture; Khan-style tablet drawings > PowerPoint; faster-talking instructors more engaging (enthusiasm proxy); pre-produced > recycled classroom lectures.\n\n**Wilson & Korn (2007)** (http://www.ministryoftruth.me.uk/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/WilsonKorn2007-Attention.pdf) debunked the \"10-minute attention span\" as folk-empirical, but engagement and re-watch rates *do* decline measurably with length. For ADHD specifically \u2014 given working-memory load \u2014 short segmentation is conservatively wise.\n\n**Richard Mayer's Cognitive Theory of Multimedia Learning** (Mayer 2001/2021, *Multimedia Learning*, Cambridge UP) \u2014 12 design principles. Most relevant: **Segmenting Principle** (https://www.cambridge.org/core/books/abs/multimedia-learning/segmenting-principle/37240877DDA0362355ADB39936027982) \u2014 \"people learn better when a multimedia message is presented in user-paced segments.\" Plus the Coherence, Modality, Signaling principles (https://www.digitallearninginstitute.com/blog/mayers-principles-multimedia-learning).\n\n**Design implications:** Cap every video at 6 min, every reading at ~600 words / 3 min, every session at ~25 min. User-paced \"Continue\" controls, not autoplay. Khan-style \"draw on screen while talking\" > slides.\n\n### Gamification that actually works\n\n**Self-Determination Theory** (Deci & Ryan; https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination_theory) \u2014 three innate needs: **autonomy, competence, relatedness.** Ryan, Rigby & Przybylski (2006) showed games engage precisely because they satisfy all three. Crucially, Deci, Koestner & Ryan's 1999 meta-analysis shows **external rewards for an already-interesting task undermine intrinsic motivation** (the overjustification effect) \u2014 why most cargo-cult points-and-badges gamification fails.\n\n**Yu-kai Chou's Octalysis Framework** (https://yukaichou.com/gamification-examples/octalysis-gamification-framework/) \u2014 8 core drives, distinguishing \"White Hat\" (empowering, intrinsic) from \"Black Hat\" (urgency, loss aversion \u2014 effective but burnout-prone). Stack White Hat drives.\n\n**Progress bars** \u2014 **Nunes & Dr\u00e8ze (2006)**, \"The Endowed Progress Effect,\" *J Consumer Research* 32(4): 504\u2013512 (https://academic.oup.com/jcr/article-abstract/32/4/504/1787425). In the famous car-wash card study, an 8-stamp card converted to a 10-stamp card with 2 \"free\" stamps **doubled completion rates.** The **Zeigarnik effect** (1927) \u2014 open loops nag memory \u2014 explains why half-complete bars pull return visits.\n\n**Streaks** \u2014 Duolingo's product team (https://www.justanotherpm.com/blog/the-psychology-behind-duolingos-streak-feature) documented that streaks + \"streak freezes\" / \"earn back\" massively increased DAU retention. Users who *chose* their own streak goal retained better than those given a default \u2014 autonomy at work.\n\n**Flow** (Csikszentmihalyi 1990, https://positivepsychology.com/mihaly-csikszentmihalyi-father-of-flow/) requires clear goals, immediate feedback, and challenge *just above* current skill. Too easy = boredom; too hard = anxiety.\n\n**Design implications:** Give Daniel real choices (which project, which flavor). Pace each module noticeably harder than the last. Visible progress bar with **prefilled progress**. Streaks **leniently** \u2014 allow a weekly \"freeze.\" Immediate, specific feedback (passing test, green check). Every reward maps to a meaningful capability gained.\n\n### Analogies + dual coding\n\n**Allan Paivio's Dual Coding Theory** (1971; https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dual-coding_theory) \u2014 the brain has two semi-independent channels (verbal + visual/imagery); info encoded in *both* is far more retrievable. Clark & Paivio (1991), \"Dual Coding Theory and Education,\" *Educational Psychology Review* 3(3): 149\u2013210 (https://nschwartz.yourweb.csuchico.edu/Clark%20&%20Paivio.pdf) extended this to instruction.\n\n**Lakoff & Johnson's *Metaphors We Live By*** (1980, https://press.uchicago.edu/ucp/books/book/chicago/M/bo3637992.html) showed our abstract conceptual system is *fundamentally* metaphorical. For technical concepts: a learner who grasps \"variables are *boxes* you put values into\" can reason about the abstract via the concrete.\n\nFor ADHD/visual learners, dual coding is doubly powerful \u2014 visuals create the novelty hit that recruits dopamine, and pictures + concrete metaphors offload working memory.\n\n**Practitioner exemplars:**\n- **Julia Evans / Wizard Zines** (https://wizardzines.com/) \u2014 comic-format zines on Linux/networking/Git.\n- **Aditya Bhargava, *Grokking Algorithms*** (Manning, 2016) \u2014 every algorithm hand-drawn; binary search introduced as a guessing game.\n- **Maggie Appleton's** illustrated essays (https://maggieappleton.com/).\n\n**Design implications:** Every new abstract concept opens with a concrete physical analogy. Pair words with diagram/sketch \u2014 never word-only. **Use Daniel's TV-production world as the analogy source**: a database query = searching the media archive; an API = handing a freelancer a brief; async code = cueing B-roll while A-roll plays. Have Daniel draw his own diagram of new concepts (generation effect + dual coding compounded).\n\n### Interleaving > blocked practice\n\n**Doug Rohrer & Kelli Taylor (2007)**, \"The Shuffling of Mathematics Practice Problems,\" *Instructional Science* 35: 481\u2013498 (http://uweb.cas.usf.edu/~drohrer/pdfs/Interleaved_Mathematics_Practice_Guide.pdf) \u2014 students who interleaved volume problems crushed blocked-practice peers on delayed tests. Taylor & Rohrer (2010), *Applied Cognitive Psychology* 24: 837\u2013848 \u2014 interleaving *doubled* delayed-test scores even when spacing was held constant. Why: interleaving forces learners to identify *which strategy applies* \u2014 the hardest and most useful step in real-world problem-solving. Blocked practice telegraphs the strategy.\n\n**Design implications:** Mix problem types within exercise sets. After teaching `if` + `for` + array methods, give exercises that *randomly* require any of the three. Mix in problems from prior weeks. Warn Daniel: \"This will feel slower and harder \u2014 that's the point.\"\n\n### Project-based learning + \"learn in public\"\n\nBrown, Collins & Duguid (1989), \"Situated Cognition and the Culture of Learning,\" *Educational Researcher* 18(1): 32\u201342 (https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.3102/0013189X018001032) \u2014 the foundational argument that knowledge is inseparable from the activity and context in which it's used. They proposed **cognitive apprenticeship** \u2014 learners do authentic tasks alongside experts.\n\n**Shawn \"swyx\" Wang's \"Learn in Public\"** (https://www.swyx.io/learn-in-public) \u2014 developers should \"create learning exhaust\" *while* learning, not after. Mechanisms: generation effect (Slamecka & Graf 1978), prot\u00e9g\u00e9 effect, compounding feedback from strangers, portfolio = career capital.\n\nFor ADHD: tangible output = salience signal (Volkow); deadlines + audience = INCUP urgency; choice of project = SDT autonomy; visible progress = endowed progress.\n\n**Design implications:** Every module ends with a tiny shipped artifact \u2014 gist, tweet, repo, devlog. Capstone = a real tool Daniel will *actually use* (script breakdown automator, footage logger). Encourage a one-line-a-day public learning journal. Avoid contrived fizzbuzz; favor micro-projects with visible output.\n\n---\n\n## Part 4 \u2014 Curriculum sequencing principles\n\n### Scaffolding & ZPD\n\nVygotsky's ZPD (1978, *Mind in Society*) describes the gap between unaided and assisted performance. **Wood, Bruner & Ross (1976)**, \"The Role of Tutoring in Problem Solving,\" *J Child Psychology and Psychiatry* 17(2): 89\u2013100 coined \"scaffolding\" with six tutor functions: recruitment, reduction of degrees of freedom, direction maintenance, marking critical features, frustration control, demonstration (https://www.simplypsychology.org/zone-of-proximal-development.html).\n\n**Applied scaffolds in programming pedagogy:**\n- **Parsons problems** (rearranging shuffled code) reduce degrees of freedom \u2014 learners do logic only, not syntax.\n- **Worked examples with fading prompts** (Sweller & Cooper 1985) reduce extraneous load while showing pattern.\n- **REPL-driven learning** (Scrimba, Boot.dev) provides contingent feedback.\n- For ADHD, scaffolds should be visible (checklists, step trackers) and contingent \u2014 added when stuck, removed when fluent.\n\n### Spiral curriculum\n\nBruner (*The Process of Education*, 1960): *\"Any subject can be taught in some intellectually honest form to any child at any stage.\"* Concepts are revisited at increasing depth (https://thirdspacelearning.com/blog/spiral-curriculum/). Beats linear \"cover-once\" approaches because each loop leverages spacing + retrieval (Roediger & Karpicke) and enables concreteness fading.\n\n**Application to Daniel's stack:**\n- **Functions** \u2014 loop 1: \"named recipes with inputs and outputs\"; loop 2: parameters/defaults/returns; loop 3: higher-order with async callbacks; loop 4: closures only when needed for an n8n custom function.\n- **Async** \u2014 loop 1: \"the API takes a second, wait\"; loop 2: Promises with `.then` when using `fetch`; loop 3: `async/await` for the Claude wrapper; loop 4: `Promise.all` for batching transcripts.\n- **JSON** \u2014 loop 1: labeled buckets; loop 2: REST response; loop 3: `stringify`/`parse`; loop 4: typed object in TS.\n\n### Cognitive Load Theory\n\n**John Sweller (1988)**, *Cognitive Science* 12: 257\u2013285. Working memory \u2248 4 elements (Cowan 2001); long-term memory is vast. Three load types:\n- **Intrinsic** \u2014 inherent complexity \u00d7 prior knowledge.\n- **Extraneous** \u2014 imposed by poor design (split attention, redundancy).\n- **Germane** \u2014 productive effort building schemas.\n\n**Key effects:**\n- **Worked-example effect** (Sweller & Cooper 1985) \u2014 novices learn more from complete solutions than unaided solving.\n- **Expertise reversal effect** (Kalyuga et al. 2003, *Educational Psychologist* 38(1)) \u2014 supports that help novices *hurt* experts; worked examples must **fade** to problem-solving.\n- **Modality effect** \u2014 visual + auditory > text + visual.\n- **Split-attention** \u2014 keep related elements (code + explanation) adjacent.\n- **Redundancy** \u2014 don't narrate text already on screen verbatim.\n\n**ADHD implications:** ADHD chronically reduces working memory capacity (https://ot4adhd.com/2022/09/05/working-memory-the-key-to-unlocking-potential-in-learners-with-adhd/). Aggressively minimize extraneous load: one concept per lesson, no tab-switching across docs, spoken+visual modality, externalize memory with cheat sheets and persistent \"what we've built\" notes.\n\n### Mastery learning + Bloom's 2-sigma\n\nBloom's \"Learning for Mastery\" (1968): students must reach ~85\u201390% on each unit before advancing; failure blamed on instruction. Bloom's 1984 \"2 Sigma Problem\" \u2014 one-on-one mastery tutoring produced ~2\u03c3 gains over conventional classroom (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloom's_2_sigma_problem). *Caveat:* later meta-analyses (https://nintil.com/bloom-sigma/) find 0.4\u20131.0\u03c3 \u2014 principle sound, magnitude debated.\n\nKhan Academy operationalizes mastery at scale \u2014 infinite re-attempts, adaptive recommendations. Launch School is the canonical mastery-based coding school (https://public.launchschool.com/pedagogy).\n\n**Checkpoint quiz design:** 3\u20135 questions per micro-lesson; mix recall (\"what does `await` do?\"), application (\"what does this code print?\"), and transfer (\"write a function that...\"). ~80% to advance. Failed attempts \u2192 targeted re-explanation, not just re-quiz.\n\n### Concrete-to-abstract (concreteness fading)\n\nBruner's enactive \u2192 iconic \u2192 symbolic, refined empirically by **Goldstone & Son (2005)**, *J Learning Sciences* 14(1): 69\u2013110 \u2014 transfer best when learners start concrete and visual concreteness progressively *fades* toward abstract symbols. **McNeil & Fyfe (2012)**, *Learning and Instruction* 22(6): 440\u2013448 \u2014 three-stage (concrete \u2192 fading \u2192 abstract) beat either extreme on transfer at three time points.\n\n**Application to programming concepts:**\n- **Function:** Stage 1: coffee machine \u2014 beans in, coffee out, `makeCoffee(beans)`. Stage 2: `formatTitle(rawTitle)` on real video metadata. Stage 3: higher-order, composition.\n- **API:** Stage 1: waiter takes your order, kitchen makes it, waiter brings response. Stage 2: real curl + JSON. Stage 3: REST verbs, status codes, OAuth.\n- **Async/await:** Stage 1: order coffee, sit at table while it's made, barista calls your name. Stage 2: real `await fetch(...)` with delay. Stage 3: Promise internals, microtask queue.\n\n### Backward design (Wiggins & McTighe)\n\n***Understanding by Design*** (1998, ASCD) \u2014 three stages: (1) identify desired results / transfer goals; (2) determine acceptable evidence; (3) only then plan learning experiences (https://teaching.uic.edu/cate-teaching-guides/syllabus-course-design/backward-design/). Three-layer prioritization: worth being familiar with \u2192 important to know \u2192 enduring understandings.\n\n**Application to Daniel:**\n- **Desired transfer goal:** Daniel can read an automation requirement, decompose it into steps, and direct Claude Code to implement and debug it.\n- **Enduring understandings:** programs are deterministic recipes; systems talk via APIs/JSON/webhooks; credentials are secrets; async work has timing; errors must be caught; version control is your safety net.\n- **Out of scope:** deep OOP, algorithm performance, hand-coded data structures.\n\n### Lesson structure templates\n\n**Madeline Hunter's seven steps** (1982, *Mastery Teaching*, https://thesecondprinciple.com/essential-teaching-skills/models-of-teaching/madeline-hunter-lesson-plan-model/): anticipatory set \u2192 objective/purpose \u2192 input \u2192 modeling \u2192 checking for understanding \u2192 guided practice \u2192 independent practice.\n\n**Gradual Release of Responsibility** (\"I do, we do, you do\") \u2014 Pearson & Gallagher (1983), extended by Fisher & Frey (2013) to four phases: focused \u2192 guided \u2192 collaborative \u2192 independent (https://keystoliteracy.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/frey_douglas_and_nancy_frey-_gradual_release_of_responsibility_intructional_framework.pdf). Common pitfall: skipping the \"we do\" collaborative phase.\n\n**Recommended micro-lesson template for Daniel (\u226425 min):**\n1. **Hook** (1 min): \"Today you'll get Claude to summarize a transcript automatically.\"\n2. **Goal** (30 sec): one explicit learning objective + mastery criterion.\n3. **Concept via analogy** (2\u20133 min): TV-production metaphor first.\n4. **Demonstration (I do)** (3\u20135 min): write the code while talking.\n5. **Guided practice (We do)** (5\u20138 min): same code with fill-in-the-blank or Parsons-problem scaffolds; each new example removes one prompt.\n6. **Independent practice (You do)** (5\u201310 min): new but isomorphic problem.\n7. **Checkpoint quiz** (2\u20133 min): 3\u20135 items; \u226580%.\n8. **Reflection prompt** (1 min): \"In your own words, when would you forget `await`?\"\n\nPredictable rhythm matters for ADHD \u2014 same template every time reduces orientation load.\n\n---\n\n## Part 5 \u2014 Synthesis: recommended module sequence for Daniel\n\nThe order below applies backward design (transfer goal first), front-loads mental models, teaches JS deeply before Python, and gates each phase behind a mastery checkpoint. Each module is \u226425 min in chunks of \u22646-min videos / 600-word readings.\n\n**Phase 0 \u2014 Mental models (no code yet)**\n1. **How computers/files/programs work** \u2014 analogous to a Premiere project. Foundational schemas without which every later abstraction is unanchored.\n2. **What is code? Programs as recipes** \u2014 variables, conditionals, loops, functions taught language-agnostically (CS50 Week 0 approach).\n3. **Command-line basics** \u2014 `ls`, `cd`, pipes, env vars. Prerequisite for Git, n8n, Playwright, 1Password CLI, Python.\n\n**Phase 1 \u2014 Data and the web (still no language)**\n4. **JSON & data structures** \u2014 concrete: a Notion page expressed as JSON. Underpins every API call.\n5. **HTTP / REST APIs / how APIs work** \u2014 hands-on with `curl` or Postman, no language yet. Concrete waiter analogy.\n\n**Phase 2 \u2014 Version control (safety net)**\n6. **Git/GitHub basics** \u2014 init, add, commit, push, branch, revert. Per Odin/Launch School/Boot.dev consensus, install before non-trivial coding.\n\n**Phase 3 \u2014 First language: JavaScript**\n7. **JavaScript fundamentals** \u2014 values, variables, functions, arrays, objects, conditionals, loops, errors.\n8. **Async / promises / await** \u2014 introduced just before he needs to call an API. Concreteness fading from \"wait for coffee\" through `.then` to `async/await`. Will be spiraled at every later module.\n9. **TypeScript additions** \u2014 types, interfaces, narrowing. The killer move for an AI-directed builder: TS catches the ~94% type errors LLMs introduce.\n\n**Phase 4 \u2014 Credentials & first real API**\n10. **OAuth + credentials/secrets (1Password CLI, env vars)** \u2014 *before* calling any API. Habit-forming.\n11. **Working with Claude API + Vercel AI SDK** \u2014 Daniel's first real automation: a script that summarizes input text. Highest motivation lift; tied directly to transfer goal.\n\n**Phase 5 \u2014 Browser & event automation**\n12. **Playwright (browser automation)** \u2014 needs JS + async. Concrete: pulling data from a web UI Daniel uses (Fireside.fm, RightNow Media).\n13. **Webhooks, cron, scheduling** \u2014 what triggers an automation. Needed before n8n flows make sense.\n\n**Phase 6 \u2014 Python (narrow, Whisper-only)**\n14. **Python crash course** \u2014 syntax delta from JS, virtualenv, pip. Don't re-teach loops/functions \u2014 leverage JS schemas. Expertise reversal in action: fewer worked examples needed.\n15. **Whisper / speech-to-text concepts** \u2014 what it is, what it costs, which flavor (faster-whisper / WhisperX / WhisperKit), output shape (SRT/VTT).\n\n**Phase 7 \u2014 Persistence & orchestration**\n16. **SQL & SQLite basics** \u2014 schemas, SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE, light joins. Concrete: a table tracking processed videos.\n17. **n8n workflows** \u2014 visual wrappers over HTTP/JSON/cron he already understands. Custom JS nodes when needed.\n\n**Phase 8 \u2014 Ops literacy (conceptual)**\n18. **Docker (conceptual only)** \u2014 what an image/container is, why it exists, why NOT on his media server. No Dockerfile authoring.\n19. **FTPS / file transfer protocols** \u2014 moving rendered files to StreamHoster. FTPS vs SFTP vs FTP clarified.\n20. **Monitoring (UptimeRobot, ntfy)** \u2014 heartbeat checks, push notifications when a flow fails.\n\n**Phase 9 \u2014 Capstone**\n21. **Putting it all together: directing Claude Code to build the system** \u2014 Daniel writes specs, decomposes problems, supervises an AI agent, debugs failures, commits work. The transfer task.\n\n### Cross-cutting design rules baked into every module\n\n- **Spiral revisits:** functions, async, error handling, JSON appear in every phase, deepening each time.\n- **Worked-example fading:** early modules show complete code; mid-curriculum, fade to fill-in-the-blank; capstone, Daniel directs only with specs.\n- **Concreteness fading:** every concept opens with a media-production analogy (Premiere bin, FTP drop, transcript file) before generalizing.\n- **Mastery checkpoints:** 3\u20135 question quiz at end of each module; <80% triggers re-explanation path.\n- **Micro-lessons \u226425 min** using the Hunter/GRR template.\n- **External memory aids:** cheat sheet PDF per module; persistent \"what we've built so far\" doc; standardized project structure.\n- **Public artifact per module:** gist, tweet, repo, devlog \u2014 every module ships something.\n\n### Suggested 5\u201310 hour core path (matches Daniel's budget)\n\n| Topic | Time | Anchor resource |\n|---|---|---|\n| Pre-flight: All 7 Fireship \"in 100 Seconds\" videos back-to-back | 20 min | Fireship channel |\n| Git | 1.5 hr | Fireship Git 100s + freeCodeCamp Gwen Faraday crash course |\n| REST APIs + JSON | 1.5 hr | MDN HTTP + first hour of Craig Dennis \"APIs for Beginners\" + Postman Beginner Path |\n| Python (Whisper-scoped) | 2 hr | Automate the Boring Stuff chapters 1\u20136 |\n| JavaScript conceptually | 1.5 hr | Mosh 1-hour + Fireship \"100+ JS concepts\" |\n| TypeScript | 1 hr | Fireship TS 100s + first half of Pocock's Beginner's Tutorial |\n| SQL | 1 hr | SQLBolt lessons 1\u20136 + Fireship 7 Database Paradigms |\n| OAuth | 1 hr | Nate Barbettini's \"OAuth in plain English\" |\n| **Core total** | **~10 hrs** | |\n\nOptional deeper-dive lessons (n8n masterclass, Vercel AI SDK 16-lesson tutorial, Playwright + MCP, WhisperX deep-dive, Docker conceptual) extend beyond the core budget.\n\n---\n\n## Caveats and source-quality flags\n\n- **The 2-sigma effect's magnitude is contested** \u2014 newer meta-analyses suggest 0.4\u20131.0\u03c3, not 2.0\u03c3. The mastery-learning principle is sound; don't overpromise the magnitude.\n- **Scaffolding's empirical base** (Wood et al. 1976) was N=32 \u2014 operationally useful but more heuristic than law-like.\n- **CLT effects** (worked-example, modality, expertise reversal) are among the best-replicated in educational psychology \u2014 highest confidence.\n- **The \"10-minute attention myth\"** was debunked by Wilson & Korn 2007. The 6-min figure from Guo et al. is solid for *video engagement* specifically, not generalized attention.\n- **Body doubling** has strong anecdotal/clinical endorsement (CHADD, ADDitude) but no large RCTs yet.\n- **Duolingo streak data** comes from company-disclosed product talks (Lenny's Podcast / Jackson Shuttleworth), not peer-reviewed RCTs \u2014 directional but not gold-standard.\n- **The \"TED Talk 18-min\" rule** is editorial (Chris Anderson), not empirical.\n- **AssemblyAI's blog posts** are technically excellent but commercially biased against self-hosted Whisper. Read with that lens.\n- **\"Master n8n in 2 Hours\" / 5\u20136 hour course channels** skew toward agency lead-gen / Skool upsells. Prefer official + Nate Herk + Leon van Zyl.\n- **No \"Playwright in 100 Seconds\" or \"OAuth in 100 Seconds\" or \"Whisper in 100 Seconds\"** Fireship videos exist as of June 2026. Substitutes noted above (Auth0 100s for OAuth-adjacent; Bouchard 6-min for Whisper; Playwright docs \"Why\" page).\n- **Anthropic Academy** is the strongest official offering and the single best place to invest learning time for Daniel's stated goal of directing Claude Code.\n\nThis dossier gives you verified URLs, specific video titles with creators, the genuine technical reasoning behind every stack choice (with TV-producer analogies you can reuse verbatim), a research-grounded set of ADHD-friendly design principles, and a sequenced module list \u2014 everything needed to author the interactive HTML curriculum.",
