      "content": "# GSR Automation v2 Curriculum Research: The Gap Dossier\n\nThis dossier covers ONLY the new/gap stack components (React, Next.js App Router, Tailwind, shadcn/ui, Radix, PostgreSQL specifics, RLS, Supabase, Zod, MCP, Anthropic Node SDK, Vercel, Node/npm, ESLint, ffmpeg, fswatch, Python email stdlib) plus a revised module sequence. **Prior research** on TypeScript fundamentals, generic Python, Git basics, generic SQL, OAuth, Claude API basics, Whisper, 1Password CLI, and the ADHD/learning-science framework is intentionally not duplicated here \u2014 only their points of contact with the new stack.\n\n---\n\n## 1. The single most important meta-finding\n\nLLM training data lags reality. For two tools in this stack, that lag actively bites a non-developer directing AI:\n\n- **Next.js**: Claude/Cursor/Copilot default to the **Pages Router** (`pages/`, `getServerSideProps`, `pages/api/...`). Daniel's stack is **App Router only**. Every Next.js prompt needs to include: *\"Next.js 16 App Router. No `pages/` directory. Async Server Components. Server Actions for mutations. `app/api/*/route.ts` for route handlers.\"* Next.js now ships an official guide at `nextjs.org/docs/app/guides` specifically for *\"configuring your Next.js project so AI coding agents use up-to-date documentation instead of outdated training data\"* \u2014 bookmark it.\n- **Supabase Auth**: AI tools love the deprecated `@supabase/auth-helpers-nextjs` package (`createServerComponentClient`, `createBrowserSupabaseClient`). The current path is `@supabase/ssr` with `createBrowserClient` / `createServerClient` and cookie-based sessions read in Server Components.\n\nThese two corrections, repeated every session, prevent ~80% of the avoidable pain.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Layer 1 \u2014 Front-end\n\n### React\n\n**Best free resources (verified):**\n\n- **react.dev/learn** \u2014 the official, rewritten-in-2023 tutorial. The companion Tic-Tac-Toe (~1\u20132 hrs) is the ideal first concrete win. Only modern hooks; the *\"You Might Not Need an Effect\"* chapter is the single best mental-model page on the internet.\n- **Scrimba \u2014 Learn React (free portion, ~5\u20136 hrs)** at `scrimba.com/learn-react-c0e`. Bob Ziroll's interactive \"scrims\" let you pause the video and edit code inline. *This is the highest-ROI ADHD format in the entire curriculum* \u2014 short loops, no setup tax, instant feedback.\n- **freeCodeCamp Learn React (Bob Ziroll, 12hr YouTube) + handbook** \u2014 `freecodecamp.org/news/free-react-course-2022/`. Same instructor as Scrimba; project-based (AirBnB clone, meme generator, Tenzies).\n- **Josh Comeau's free blog articles** (`joshwcomeau.com`) \u2014 *\"Why React Re-Renders\"*, *\"Demystifying useEffect\"*, *\"An Interactive Guide to JavaScript Events\"*. Mental-model focus, perfect for someone supervising AI code.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"React in 100 Seconds\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=Tn6-PIqc4UM` (~2 min). Day-one watch.\n- **Web Dev Simplified (Kyle Cook)** \u2014 `youtube.com/@WebDevSimplified`. Clear \"the why\" explainers in 20\u201340 min chunks.\n- **Jack Herrington \u2014 Intro to React playlist** \u2014 `youtube.com/@jherr/videos`. Modern, practical, free, naturally transitions into Next.js.\n\n**Why React over alternatives (Vue, Svelte, Angular, vanilla JS):**\n\n1. **Component model + ecosystem dominance.** Almost any UI pattern has a battle-tested implementation. React docs frame this as the design intent: components composed by *\"independent people, teams, and organizations\"*.\n2. **AI training-data prevalence is the practical kicker for an AI-directed workflow.** Claude/Cursor/Copilot are dramatically more accurate on React than on Svelte/Solid/Qwik because public training data leans React-heavy. Lee Robinson confirms this is exactly why he uses React + Tailwind: *\"It works great with AI / v0.\"*\n3. **Stability + meta-investment.** React is tested on Meta surfaces with 1B+ users and 100k+ components per commit.\n4. **vs vanilla JS:** declarative, state-driven re-rendering replaces hand-rolled DOM manipulation \u2014 the original problem React was built to solve.\n\n**TV/media analogies:** Components = reusable lower-thirds templates (designed once, instanced per segment with different props). State = \"is this graphic currently animated in?\" \u2014 the screen re-draws when state changes, exactly like an Avid MOS plugin reacting to a newsroom update. Props vs state = scripted rundown sheet (props) vs live-input data (state).\n\n**Caveats:** Skip anything using `class` components, `componentDidMount`, the legacy context API, or Create React App (CRA was deprecated by the React team in 2023; the modern path is Vite or a framework like Next.js).\n\n---\n\n### Next.js 16 App Router\n\n**Best free resources (App-Router-confirmed):**\n\n- **Official Next.js Learn \u2014 \"Next.js Foundations\" / Dashboard App** \u2014 `nextjs.org/learn/dashboard-app`. Confirmed App-Router-based (the URL breadcrumb literally says \"App Router\"). ~6\u201310 hrs self-paced, ~16 chapters covering styling (Tailwind), nested routing, streaming, Server Actions, mutations, auth, deployment. **This is the canonical course \u2014 by the Next.js team itself.**\n- **Official Next.js Learn \u2014 \"React Foundations\"** \u2014 `nextjs.org/learn/react-foundations`. Explicitly teaches Server Components and Suspense; use as a prerequisite if React fundamentals are shaky.\n- **App Router docs** \u2014 `nextjs.org/docs/app`. Critical: the docs have a router-mode toggle at the top of the sidebar \u2014 always select \"App Router.\"\n- **Jack Herrington's Pro Next.js free tutorials** \u2014 `pronextjs.dev/tutorials`. Jack states explicitly: *\"In this course, we are going to be covering the app router exclusively\u2026 the App Router is the new standard for Next.js.\"*\n- **freeCodeCamp Ticketing App (Jacob Lower)** \u2014 `freecodecamp.org/news/use-next-js-tailwind-css-and-mongodb-to-build-a-ticketing-application/`. ~2hr YouTube; App Router + Tailwind.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"Next.js in 100 Seconds + Beginner's Tutorial\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=Sklc_fQBmcs`. \u26a0\ufe0f **Use only the 100-second intro for the conceptual hook**; the tutorial portion uses Pages Router (verified \u2014 `pages/index.js`, `pages/api/hello.js`).\n- **Lee Robinson (Vercel) \u2014 \"The New Next.js App Router\"** \u2014 on the Vercel YouTube channel `youtube.com/@VercelHQ`. ~27 min; official intro by the platform's VP of DevX.\n- **Jack Herrington \u2014 Pro Next.js series (App Router only)** \u2014 `youtube.com/@jherr/videos`.\n- **Theo \u2014 \"Giving Up On Next.js\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=9jqPbNgzHOA`. Critical App-Router take; useful so Daniel hears tradeoffs.\n\n**Why Next.js over plain React (Vite/CRA):**\n\n1. **Routing, SSR, image/font optimization, and data fetching are built in.** The official framing: *\"A framework can solve these problems.\"*\n2. **Server Components + Server Actions = full-stack in one codebase.** Database query and UI in the same file. Lee Robinson: *\"Next.js enabled me to write my entire application in one programming language\u2026 now it's even easier with React Server Components, Server Actions.\"*\n3. **Deployment story (Vercel) is one-click** with per-PR preview URLs.\n4. **Co-creation with React core.** Vercel literally co-builds new React APIs (RSC, Server Actions, Transitions) *in* Next.js before they hit stable React \u2014 so Next.js gets new React features first.\n\n**Why App Router specifically over Pages Router:**\n\n1. **Server Components by default** \u2014 database queries co-locate with UI, less JS shipped, free SEO.\n2. **Nested layouts + streaming** \u2014 Pages Router had no top-level data fetching for shared layouts; App Router does. Lee Robinson: *\"This was not possible before in the pages router.\"*\n3. **The future direction.** Pages Router is in legacy maintenance; App Router is on React 19 + canary.\n4. **End-to-end type safety + global data fetching.** Lee Robinson: *\"No end-to-end type safety? No global data fetching? The App Router is so much nicer in this regard.\"*\n\n**Why server components / server actions / route handlers:**\n\n- **Server Components** solve the bundle-size and waterfall problem of client-side React. Pre-RSC you needed a REST endpoint + a client component + a fetcher hook. Now it's one async function.\n- **Server Actions** let a button-click invoke a server function directly via the `\"use server\"` directive \u2014 form mutations without writing an API route.\n- **Route Handlers** replace `pages/api/*.js`. Located at `app/api/*/route.ts`, returning Web-standard `Response` objects.\n\n**TV/media analogies:**\n- Next.js = a fully-equipped studio (cameras, lights, audio board, teleprompter, satellite uplink). Plain React (Vite) = renting an empty soundstage and bringing your own gear.\n- App Router vs Pages Router = newer IP/SDI broadcast workflow vs older tape-based \u2014 both ship a show, but new productions almost never start on the old workflow because the new one composes better with modern tools.\n- Server Components = pre-rendered title cards / character generator pre-rolls (baked, ready, shipped). Client Components = live graphics overlays that react to user input on air.\n- Server Actions = a button on the production switcher that fires a macro on the server \u2014 no separate API endpoint to wire up.\n\n**Source-quality caveats:** Flag any tutorial that uses a `pages/` directory, `getServerSideProps`/`getStaticProps`, `_app.js`/`_document.js`, or was published before May 2023 (App Router went stable in 13.4). Maximilian Schwarzm\u00fcller's Academind course covers both routers \u2014 fine, but pick the App Router modules.\n\n---\n\n### Tailwind CSS\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Official Tailwind docs** \u2014 `tailwindcss.com/docs`. Searchable utility reference; every utility has a live example.\n- **Tailwind Play** \u2014 `play.tailwindcss.com`. Zero-install playground \u2014 ideal for the \"ask Claude for a snippet, paste, iterate\" workflow.\n- **Adam Wathan \u2014 \"CSS Utility Classes and Separation of Concerns\"** \u2014 `adamwathan.me/css-utility-classes-and-separation-of-concerns/`. The original 2017 manifesto; still the best \"why\" article.\n- **Tailwind v4 launch post** \u2014 `tailwindcss.com/blog/tailwindcss-v4`. Critical because v4 (Jan 2025) changed the install model significantly.\n\n**Tailwind v4 changes to know:**\n- CSS-first config: no more `tailwind.config.js`. Configure via `@theme {}` in CSS.\n- One-line install: `@import \"tailwindcss\";` \u2014 no more `@tailwind base/components/utilities` directives.\n- New Rust-based \"Oxide\" engine \u2014 ~5\u00d7 faster builds.\n- First-party Vite plugin `@tailwindcss/vite`.\n- Automatic content detection (no `content` array).\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"Tailwind in 100 Seconds\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=mr15Xzb1Ook`.\n- **Net Ninja \u2014 Tailwind playlist** \u2014 `youtube.com/playlist?list=PL4cUxeGkcC9gpXORlEHjc5bgnIi5HEGhw`. ~1.5 hr; \u26a0\ufe0f setup is pre-v4 so pair with current install docs.\n- **freeCodeCamp Tailwind + Next.js ticketing app** \u2014 `freecodecamp.org/news/use-next-js-tailwind-css-and-mongodb-to-build-a-ticketing-application/`.\n\n**Why Tailwind over plain CSS / CSS Modules / styled-components:**\n\n1. **No naming bikeshedding.** Adam Wathan's argument: semantic class names (`.author-bio__name`) couple CSS to HTML structure anyway, so the \"separation of concerns\" payoff is illusory.\n2. **System values reduce magic numbers.** Tailwind ships a constrained design scale (spacing, color, type) \u2014 a built-in design system.\n3. **AI tools generate Tailwind exceptionally well.** Lee Robinson: *\"It was easy for me to pick up, stays consistent whenever I revisit old projects, and works great with AI / v0.\"* Vercel's v0 outputs Tailwind by default.\n4. **vs styled-components/Emotion:** Tailwind is zero-runtime \u2014 styles compiled at build time, not generated on the client. CSS-in-JS adds JS bundle weight and runtime cost.\n5. **vs plain CSS / CSS Modules:** no context-switching between files, no naming, no specificity wars.\n\n**TV/media analogies:** Tailwind = the show's brand kit / style guide \u2014 pre-defined palette, type scale, spacing. Plain CSS = re-mixing the brand colors on every shot. Tailwind Play = the multiviewer / preview monitor \u2014 iterate live before going to air.\n\n**Caveats:** Flag tutorials using `tailwind.config.js` for theming without mentioning the v4 `@theme {}` approach, `@tailwind base/components/utilities` directives (v3 syntax), or the `purge:` option (v2 syntax \u2014 fully automatic in v4).\n\n---\n\n### shadcn/ui\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Official docs Introduction** \u2014 `ui.shadcn.com/docs`. THE canonical \"this is NOT a component library\" explanation. Lists the 4 principles (Open Code, Composition, Distribution, Beautiful Defaults) and an explicit *\"Works with AI\"* section: *\"The design of shadcn/ui makes it easy for AI tools to work with your code. Its open code and consistent API allow AI models to read, understand, and even generate new components.\"*\n- **Official Installation** \u2014 `ui.shadcn.com/docs/installation`. Note current CLI is `npx shadcn@latest` (renamed from `shadcn-ui@latest` in Sept 2024).\n- **Vercel Academy \u2014 shadcn/ui Course** \u2014 `vercel.com/academy/shadcn-ui/why-shadcn-ui-is-different`. Official, since shadcn now works at Vercel.\n- **freeCodeCamp Full Course** \u2014 `freecodecamp.org/news/mastering-shadcn-ui-components/`. ~3hr YouTube. Caveat: filmed before the CLI rename.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Theo \u2014 \"How Shadcn/ui ACTUALLY Works\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=AqmMx_JidGo` (~15 min). Best single explanation of why copy-paste wins.\n- **Theo \u2014 \"This might change how we build UI forever\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=c5OPn_dyNcc` (~12 min). Covers the CLI/registry \u2014 the same one Claude Code invokes.\n- **Web Dev Simplified \u2014 \"How I Built My Own Shadcn Library\"** \u2014 relevant once Daniel wants reusable blocks.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f **Fireship has no shadcn \"100 Seconds\" video as of June 2026** \u2014 don't promise one.\n\n**Why shadcn/ui over MUI / Chakra / Ant Design / Mantine:**\n\n1. **You own the code \u2014 no `node_modules` black box.** Official docs: *\"This is not a component library. It is how you build your component library.\"* MUI/Chakra/Ant ship as npm packages whose source lives in `node_modules`, which **AI tools cannot meaningfully edit** because changes get blown away on `npm install`. With shadcn, the file lives at `components/ui/button.tsx` in your repo, and Claude Code can read, rewrite, and refactor it freely.\n2. **AI-First architecture is explicit, not accidental.** This is THE reason shadcn is correct for Daniel's workflow.\n3. **Behavior (Radix) separated from styling (Tailwind in files you own)** \u2014 no fight against a Material Design or Ant aesthetic baked in.\n4. **No version-lock-in roulette.** When traditional libraries release breaking changes you're along for the ride; with shadcn you opt-in to updates via CLI diff.\n\n**Honest trade-off:** No automatic updates \u2014 but Claude Code can be told to \"check for the latest version of [component] and apply the diff.\"\n\n**TV/media analogies:** shadcn/ui = unlocked b-roll footage you license outright and re-edit in your NLE \u2014 you own the master files. MUI/Chakra = a stock-music subscription where you can adjust volume but can't change the melody. The shadcn CLI (`npx shadcn add button`) = ingesting a clip from your shared archive into your project bin.\n\n**Caveats:** CLI rename Sept 2024 (`shadcn-ui` \u2192 `shadcn`); the 3hr freeCodeCamp course pre-dates this. Some third-party \"shadcn explainers\" (Magic UI, Shadcn Studio) are content marketing for adjacent products.\n\n---\n\n### Radix UI\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Radix Primitives Introduction** \u2014 `radix-ui.com/primitives/docs/overview/introduction`. Defines \"headless / unstyled / accessible primitives.\"\n- **Radix Accessibility Overview** \u2014 `radix-ui.com/primitives/docs/overview/accessibility`. THE single most important page \u2014 explains WAI-ARIA, keyboard nav, focus management.\n- **Vercel Academy \u2014 \"What are Radix Primitives?\"** \u2014 `vercel.com/academy/shadcn-ui/what-are-radix-primitives`. Plain-English explainer: *\"Think of Radix UI primitives as the 'engine' of a component \u2014 they handle all the complex logic while remaining invisible to the user.\"*\n\n**YouTube:** Radix-specific content is thin because most people meet Radix *through* shadcn. Theo's channel covers Radix as the \"right answer\" for headless in multiple videos. Honest note: there is no canonical \"Radix in 100 seconds\" video; the docs + Vercel Academy lesson are sufficient, and every shadcn video implicitly teaches Radix.\n\n**Why Radix under the hood:**\n\n1. **Accessibility is brutally hard to implement correctly.** Radix docs: *\"We handle many of the difficult implementation details related to accessibility, including aria and role attributes, focus management, and keyboard navigation.\"* A dialog isn't just a div \u2014 it needs focus trapping, escape-key handling, screen-reader announcements, scroll locking, return-focus-on-close. Weeks of work, given to you free.\n2. **Unstyled = total visual freedom.** Compare to MUI where you fight a 200kb Material Design theme to make a button not look like Android.\n3. **Composition API.** `Dialog.Root`, `Dialog.Trigger`, `Dialog.Portal`, `Dialog.Overlay`, `Dialog.Content` \u2014 re-arrange the pieces.\n4. **Production endorsements:** Linear, Supabase, Vercel, CodeSandbox use it. Maintained by WorkOS (well-funded, stable).\n\n**TV/media analogies:** Radix = a professional audio mixing console with no faceplate \u2014 every fader and EQ band is broadcast-spec, but no paint, no labels. You bolt on your own faceplate (Tailwind classes). Accessibility logic = the closed-captioning + SAP audio tracks broadcast standards legally require \u2014 Radix is the post-production house that auto-handles compliance.\n\n**Caveat:** Radix has two products \u2014 **Primitives** (unstyled, what shadcn uses) and **Themes** (a styled library). Always specify Primitives in the curriculum.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Layer 2 \u2014 Back-end / Database\n\n### PostgreSQL specifics\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **postgresqltutorial.com** \u2014 soup-to-nuts Postgres features: JSONB, arrays, enums, CTEs, window functions, triggers, full-text search. Use as a lookup reference.\n- **Official PostgreSQL Tutorial (Part I of docs)** \u2014 `postgresql.org/docs/current/tutorial.html`. ~1\u20132hr read; written by the core team.\n- **PostgreSQL Docs \u00a75.9 \u2014 Row Security Policies** \u2014 `postgresql.org/docs/current/ddl-rowsecurity.html`. 15 min; canonical definition.\n- **freeCodeCamp \u2014 Learn PostgreSQL Full Course (Amigoscode, ~4hr)** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=qw--VYLpxG4`. Most-watched Postgres course on YouTube; Postgres-native.\n- **freeCodeCamp \u2014 PostgreSQL Course for Beginners (Cristian, ~3hr, 2024)** \u2014 `freecodecamp.org/news/posgresql-course-for-beginners/`. Newer; built-in mini-challenges fight ADHD drift.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"PostgreSQL in 100 Seconds\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=n2Fluyr3lbc`. Watch FIRST.\n\n**Why PostgreSQL over MySQL / SQLite / MongoDB:**\n\n1. **Standards compliance + advanced SQL.** Window functions, CTEs, partial indexes, materialized views, DDL inside transactions (you can ROLLBACK a CREATE TABLE).\n2. **JSONB beats Mongo at its own game.** Binary indexed JSON with GIN indexes \u2014 document-style flexibility *plus* joins, foreign keys, and transactions.\n3. **RLS is built in.** MySQL has no equivalent; emulating it with views or app-layer code is \"where security bugs live.\"\n4. **Extensibility (pgvector, PostGIS).** Daniel's AI work may need vector search later; pgvector turns Postgres into a vector DB without adding another service.\n5. **Industry momentum.** Postgres has been Stack Overflow's #1 most-admired and most-desired database three years running; OpenAI runs ChatGPT's backend on Postgres. AI coding tools have seen far more Postgres SQL than any alternative.\n6. **vs SQLite:** single file, one user \u2014 not for a web app with many editors.\n\n**TV/media analogy:** Postgres = the media archive / asset management system (Avid Interplay, Iconik). Clips (rows) live in bins (tables) with structured metadata (columns), enforced rules (constraints, foreign keys). JSONB is the \"Notes\" field \u2014 free-form but searchable. Extensions like pgvector are the AI-tagging plugins you can bolt on.\n\n**Caveat:** Many \"SQL courses\" use MySQL or SQLite syntax. Skip anything not titled \"PostgreSQL\" \u2014 Postgres differs on AUTO_INCREMENT (use `SERIAL`/`IDENTITY`), string quoting (single quotes only), JSON syntax, and OFFSET. Always tell Claude Code \"we are on Postgres\" each session.\n\n---\n\n### Row-Level Security (RLS)\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Supabase RLS Guide** \u2014 `supabase.com/docs/guides/database/postgres/row-level-security`. Enabling RLS, writing policies, `auth.uid()`, `anon` vs `authenticated` roles, helper patterns, when to use SECURITY DEFINER, view caveats (in Postgres \u226515 use `security_invoker=true`). **Read this before writing a single policy.**\n- **PostgreSQL \u00a75.9** (above) \u2014 the mechanics Supabase wraps: USING vs WITH CHECK, FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY, BYPASSRLS.\n- **Bytebase \u2014 Postgres RLS Footguns** \u2014 `bytebase.com/blog/postgres-row-level-security-footguns/`. Real-world mistakes: non-LEAKPROOF functions killing indexes, missing WITH CHECK letting users INSERT data they can't see, views silently bypassing RLS, connection-pooling making `current_user` useless.\n- **Scott Pierce \u2014 Optimizing RLS for Performance** \u2014 `scottpierce.dev/posts/optimizing-postgres-rls/`. Best write-up on wrapping policy logic in `SECURITY DEFINER STABLE` functions to avoid chained RLS sub-queries.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Net Ninja \u2014 Supabase Tutorial #10: Intro to RLS & Policies** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=WAa3a-HxLVs`. Calmest, clearest 10-min explanation.\n- **\"Supabase Row Level Security: Common Mistakes & Real Risks\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=3yDr4mrZXAw`. The exact failure mode Daniel must avoid since the browser carries the anon key.\n\n**Why RLS over application-layer authorization:**\n\n1. **Defense in depth.** When Claude Code (or a bad prompt) forgets `WHERE user_id = ?`, RLS still blocks the leak.\n2. **Consistent across all clients.** Browser, mobile, MCP, curl \u2014 all hit the same gate. App-layer auth has to be reimplemented in every codepath.\n3. **Critical when the client uses the anon key directly** (the Supabase model). The browser literally has DB keys; RLS is the only thing stopping it reading every row. *\"Leaks look like normal traffic.\"*\n4. **Auditability.** Security logic lives next to data in version-controlled SQL.\n\n**Why SQL RPCs / SECURITY DEFINER functions for atomic mutations vs read-modify-write in a route handler:**\n\n1. **Race conditions kill read-modify-write.** Two clients doing \"fetch count \u2192 +1 \u2192 write back\" can lose an increment. A single SQL function (`UPDATE counters SET n = n + 1 WHERE id = $1 RETURNING n`) runs as one atomic transaction.\n2. **Transactional atomicity over multiple tables.** \"Create order AND decrement inventory AND insert ledger row\" all succeed or all roll back.\n3. **SECURITY DEFINER lets a trusted function bypass RLS for one specific operation.** Example: a user can't read the `roles` table directly, but a `can_user_access_project()` function \u2014 defined by the `postgres` role \u2014 can, and returns just a boolean.\n4. **Performance bonus.** SECURITY DEFINER STABLE functions in policies avoid chained RLS sub-queries that scale exponentially.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f SECURITY DEFINER is sharp \u2014 Bytebase warns it runs with creator privileges, so a bug can leak data wide. Use sparingly, audit each one, keep out of exposed schemas.\n\n**Why idempotent migrations (IF NOT EXISTS, CREATE OR REPLACE):** Safe re-runs (CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS won't error on a second run); deploy resilience (half-completed migrations are recoverable by re-running); environment parity (same file runs against local, staging, production). AI-tool friendliness: when Claude Code re-generates a migration, idempotent style means the chat history of small edits compiles into one safe re-runnable file.\n\n**TV/media analogy:** RLS = access-control list on shared production drives. Editor Sarah only *sees* the folders for Project Atlas \u2014 not because the front desk hid them, but because the NAS itself refuses to list them for her account. Even a stolen keycard can't see other people's content. SECURITY DEFINER = the executive producer briefly stamping a request with director-level authority for one specific, audited approval task.\n\n---\n\n### Supabase\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Official Supabase docs** \u2014 `supabase.com/docs`. Critical sub-sections:\n  - **Server-Side Auth for Next.js** \u2014 `supabase.com/docs/guides/auth/server-side/nextjs` \u2014 the **current `@supabase/ssr` pattern**.\n  - **Creating an SSR client** \u2014 `supabase.com/docs/guides/auth/server-side/creating-a-client`.\n  - **SSR Advanced Guide** \u2014 token caching, CDN gotchas, ISR warnings.\n  - **Next.js Quickstart** \u2014 `supabase.com/docs/guides/getting-started/quickstarts/nextjs`.\n  - **Full \"Build a User Management App\" tutorial** \u2014 auth + RLS + Storage end-to-end.\n- **Supabase YouTube Crash Course playlist** \u2014 `youtube.com/playlist?list=PL4cUxeGkcC9hUb6sHthUEwG7r9VDPBMKO`. Made by the company; always matches docs.\n- **freeCodeCamp \u2014 Supabase for Beginners (2025, Sales Dashboard, 5hr)** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=Q7P20fHJlm4`. Newest comprehensive course. Covers Auth, role-based access, triggers for profile auto-creation, Realtime.\n\n**Best YouTube (with caveats):**\n\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"Supabase in 100 Seconds\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=zBZgdTb-dns`. Watch immediately after Postgres-100s.\n- **Jon Meyers \u2014 \"The Right Way to do Auth with the Next.js App Router \u2014 UPDATED\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=v6UvgfSIjQ0`. **CRITICAL \u2014 current, uses `@supabase/ssr`.** Jon Meyers (formerly Supabase DevRel) is the de-facto authority. Watch twice.\n- **Jon Meyers \u2014 Build a Twitter Clone with Next.js App Router + Supabase (egghead, free)** \u2014 `egghead.io/courses/build-a-twitter-clone-with-the-next-js-app-router-and-supabase-19bebadb`. The closest blueprint to Daniel's likely architecture.\n- **Traversy Media \u2014 Supabase Crash Course (~25 min)**. Quickest dashboard tour.\n- **Web Dev Simplified \u2014 Realtime Chat with Supabase (~2hr)**. Kyle's signature clarity.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f **OLDER Jon Meyers video to AVOID:** \"The Right Way to do Auth with the Next.js App Router\" *without* \"UPDATED\" in the title (`watch?v=VVElr2n90KY`). Uses earlier API.\n\n**Why Supabase over Firebase:**\n\n1. **SQL/Postgres vs NoSQL.** Firestore forces denormalization and client-side joins. For Daniel's relational data (productions \u2192 episodes \u2192 assets \u2192 people), Postgres is the natural fit.\n2. **Open source + self-hostable.** If Supabase sunset or raised prices, you `pg_dump` and move to AWS RDS, Neon, Railway, or your own VPS. Firebase migration is a 3\u20136 month rewrite.\n3. **RLS vs Firebase Security Rules.** Both enforce row-level access. RLS is standard SQL (composable, testable); Firebase Rules are a proprietary DSL.\n4. **Predictable pricing.** Firebase bills per read/write/delete and can spike; Supabase has tier-based pricing.\n\n**Why Supabase over raw Postgres + custom auth:** Auth alone (magic links, OAuth, password reset, JWT signing, email templates) is months of work \u2014 Supabase ships it day one with audited open-source GoTrue. Auto-generated REST + GraphQL from your schema (PostgREST) means Claude Code can talk to the DB through a stable API without you writing a backend layer. Storage, Realtime (Postgres WAL replication), Edge Functions \u2014 each would be another 2-week side quest.\n\n**Why a BaaS at all for a solo operator:** Focus on the show, not the rigging. Supabase handles backups, replication, OS updates, cert renewals, DDoS.\n\n**Why magic-link auth over passwords:**\n\n1. **Nothing to leak, forget, or brute-force.** No password DB to breach; no password reuse cascading from another site's breach.\n2. **Simpler UX for occasional users.** A producer logging in weekly doesn't remember anything; one click = signed in.\n3. **No password-reset flow to build/maintain.** The magic link itself *is* the reset flow.\n4. **Less phishable.** Users never type credentials, so a fake login page has nothing to capture.\n5. **Honest tradeoffs:** tied to email-account security (but that's already true via password reset); requires inbox context-switch; delivery delays possible. For a small trusted team, tradeoffs strongly favor magic links.\n\n**TV/media analogy:** Supabase = rented turnkey production facility \u2014 sound stages (Postgres), edit bays (Studio), tape vault (Storage), security desk (Auth/GoTrue), runners passing messages (Realtime), late-night control room (Edge Functions). Firebase = the same facility owned by a single mega-studio (Google); moving out means rebuilding everything. Supabase = the indie collective \u2014 same conveniences, but you can `pg_dump` your archive into a truck and move across town. Magic links = single-use stage passes emailed to talent.\n\n**Source-quality red flags for Supabase:**\n- \ud83d\udea9 `@supabase/auth-helpers-nextjs` (deprecated) instead of `@supabase/ssr`\n- \ud83d\udea9 `'use client'` + `supabase.auth.getUser()` in a top-level page (auth should be server-side via cookies)\n- \ud83d\udea9 Pages Router examples (`getServerSideProps`, `pages/api/...`)\n- \ud83d\udea9 `service_role` key (or `sb_secret_*`) in client code or `NEXT_PUBLIC_` env vars \u2014 that key bypasses RLS\n- \ud83d\udea9 Views over RLS-protected tables without `security_invoker=true` (Postgres \u226515) \u2014 silent data leak\n\n---\n\n### Vercel deployment\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Vercel Docs \u2014 Hobby Plan** \u2014 `vercel.com/docs/plans/hobby`\n- **Vercel Docs \u2014 Limits** \u2014 `vercel.com/docs/limits` \u2014 function durations, file counts, log retention.\n- **Vercel Pricing** \u2014 `vercel.com/pricing`\n- **Next.js Docs \u2014 Deploy to Vercel** \u2014 *\"The easiest way to deploy Next.js to production is to use the Vercel platform developed by the creators of Next.js.\"*\n\n**Current free-tier essentials (verified June 2026):**\n- 1 developer seat, **non-commercial use only** (enforced)\n- 100 GB Fast Data Transfer / month\n- 1 M Edge Requests / month\n- 1 M Function Invocations / month\n- 4 hours Active CPU / month\n- Function max duration: **60s default on Hobby** (longer on Pro)\n- Unlimited deployments, automatic HTTPS, preview deploys on every Git push\n- No payment overflow on Hobby \u2014 you hit the cap, then wait or upgrade\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Lee Robinson channel** \u2014 `youtube.com/@leerob`. Self-host, caching, server actions deep dives.\n- **Jack Herrington's free intro lesson \"The React, Next.js, and Vercel controversy\"** \u2014 `pronextjs.dev/workshops/...`. Honest framing of the tribal politics.\n- **Software Engineering Daily \u2014 Vercel AI with Lee Robinson** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=OVNH8Y2EKo8` (~45 min).\n- **Vercel official channel** \u2014 `youtube.com/@VercelHQ` \u2014 Next.js Conf talks, Vercel Ship keynotes.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f No dedicated Fireship \"Vercel in 100 Seconds\" video exists.\n\n**Why Vercel over Netlify / Cloudflare Pages / AWS Amplify / Railway / VPS:**\n\n1. **Vercel makes Next.js \u2014 first-class is literal.** New Next.js features (Server Components, Server Actions, Partial Prerendering, App Router) ship on Vercel first; others catch up months later. For an AI workflow, Claude Code writes modern Next.js, and Vercel runs it without configuration.\n2. **Preview deployments are unmatched.** Every Git push gets a unique URL automatically \u2014 the killer feature for AI-assisted dev: push, get URL, share, decide, merge.\n3. **Zero-config edge network + serverless functions.** No Nginx, PM2, Let's Encrypt, log rotation to manage.\n4. **Honest trade-offs:** bandwidth bills can spike on viral traffic; Hobby is non-commercial only; function duration is short on Hobby (60s default \u2014 long AI streaming can hit it). Cloudflare Pages is cheaper at scale; Cloudflare's Next.js support has lagged.\n\n**Why serverless functions vs long-running server:** Pay per invocation vs pay 24/7; automatic infinite scaling vs manual provisioning; cold starts (first hit slower) vs always warm; stateless (need external DB/cache) vs in-memory state OK; near-zero DevOps vs high DevOps burden.\n\n**TV/media analogies:**\n- Vercel = the broadcast distribution network \u2014 you hand over the episode, they handle CDN edge nodes (affiliates), bandwidth, SSL (broadcast encryption).\n- Preview deployments = dailies/rough-cut screening links \u2014 every push is a screener URL.\n- Edge runtime = local affiliate stations rebroadcasting from the closest tower.\n- Serverless functions = freelance crew per shoot \u2014 only pay when filming, scales to any production, but a ramp-up time at start (\"cold start\") and no memory from yesterday.\n- Long-running server = full-time staff on payroll 24/7 \u2014 instantly responsive, remembers everything, but you pay regardless and manage HR (security patches, monitoring).\n- VPS = owning your own studio + transmitter tower \u2014 maximum control, FCC paperwork is yours.\n\n**Caveats:** Pricing changes every ~6 months (April 2025 brought Fluid Compute and changed function-duration model). Always link to `vercel.com/docs/limits` directly, not third-party blogs.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Layer 3 \u2014 AI / Validation\n\n### Zod\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Official Zod docs \u2014 \"Basics\"** \u2014 `zod.dev/basics`. Auto-versioned to Zod 4; `.parse` vs `.safeParse`, `z.infer`, ZodError shape.\n- **Matt Pocock's free Zod Tutorial (Total TypeScript)** \u2014 `totaltypescript.com/tutorials/zod`. 10 interactive exercises, ~1\u20132 hrs; each lesson is a failing test you fix. ADHD-friendly micro-loops. GitHub mirror at `github.com/total-typescript/zod-tutorial`.\n- **Tim Deschryver \u2014 \"Why we should verify HTTP response bodies with Zod\"** \u2014 `timdeschryver.dev/blog/why-we-should-verify-http-response-bodies-and-why-we-should-use-zod-for-this`. Best argument for Zod at API boundaries.\n- **Cod\u00fa \u2014 \"Zod parse vs safeParse\"** \u2014 `codu.co/niall/zod-parse-versus-safeparse-what-s-the-difference-7t_tjfne`.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Web Dev Simplified \u2014 \"Learn Zod In 30 Minutes\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=L6BE-U3oy80`. The single best beginner crash course.\n- **Matt Pocock per-concept micro-videos** \u2014 embedded in the Total TypeScript tutorial; 2\u20135 min each.\n- **\"Master Zod in Just 30 Minutes\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=f-4-k1CP6wA`. Alternative pacing.\n\n\u26a0\ufe0f No verified Fireship \"Zod in 100 Seconds\" video exists.\n\n**Why Zod / runtime validation when TypeScript already gives compile-time types:**\n\nThe core insight: **TypeScript types are erased at compile time** \u2014 they don't exist when your program runs. Any data crossing a runtime boundary (HTTP response, form input, `process.env`, file contents, LLM JSON output) arrives as `unknown` no matter what TypeScript claims it \"should be.\" Zod re-establishes the type contract at the boundary by *actually inspecting the value*. From Matt Pocock's tutorial: *\"TypeScript will present an error if it's not a number, but on its own it doesn't know if a number is too low or too high\u2026 There's a similar problem with third-party API responses.\"*\n\n**Why Zod won vs Yup / Joi / io-ts / Valibot / ArkType:**\n\n1. **TS-first inference.** `type User = z.infer<typeof schema>` \u2014 one source of truth. Yup/Joi predate TS-first design, so teams maintain a schema *and* a separate interface that drift apart.\n2. **Ecosystem network effects.** Default resolver for React Hook Form, tRPC, Drizzle ORM, Next.js server actions, and \u2014 critically \u2014 **the Anthropic TypeScript SDK ships a `zodOutputFormat` helper** for structured outputs.\n3. **~20M weekly npm downloads** vs alternatives. Valibot is smaller (~1\u20133 KB gzipped vs Zod's ~13 KB) and tree-shakeable, which matters for browser bundles but not Node.js server use \u2014 exactly Daniel's case.\n4. **Joi has no native TS inference; Yup's is weaker; io-ts is functional/awkward; ArkType is newer and less integrated.**\n\n**TV/media analogy:** Zod = the QC engineer at ingest. The shooter *said* they'd deliver 4K ProRes 422 HQ at 23.976 with -20 dBFS audio. TypeScript = the email confirming the spec. **Zod = the engineer who opens the file in Resolve and verifies codec, resolution, framerate, audio levels** before anything goes to the edit bay. If it's wrong, reject it at ingest \u2014 not after the colorist spent six hours.\n\n**Caveats:** Some blog posts reference Zod 3.x error shapes (`.error.errors`); Zod 4 uses `.error.issues`. Official zod.dev reflects v4.\n\n---\n\n### MCP (Model Context Protocol)\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Anthropic's announcement, \"Introducing the Model Context Protocol\"** (Nov 25, 2024) \u2014 `anthropic.com/news/model-context-protocol`. Primary source.\n- **modelcontextprotocol.io \u2014 Introduction** \u2014 `modelcontextprotocol.io/introduction`. Where the \"USB-C port for AI applications\" framing lives. *\"A universal, open standard for connecting AI systems with data sources, replacing fragmented integrations with a single protocol.\"*\n- **Anthropic docs \u2014 MCP section** \u2014 `docs.anthropic.com/en/docs/agents-and-tools/mcp`.\n- **Wikipedia: Model Context Protocol** \u2014 concise history; ecosystem timeline (OpenAI adoption March 2025; donation to Linux Foundation Dec 2025).\n- **Pragmatic Engineer \u2014 \"MCP Protocol\"** \u2014 `newsletter.pragmaticengineer.com/p/mcp`. Long-form origin story, N\u00d7M \u2192 N+M framing, security caveats.\n- **Zuplo \u2014 \"One Year of MCP\"** \u2014 `zuplo.com/blog/one-year-of-mcp`. Adoption timeline.\n\n**Best YouTube:**\n\n- **Mahesh Murag (Anthropic) \u2014 \"Building Agents with Model Context Protocol \u2014 Full Workshop\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=kQmXtrmQ5Zg` (~2hr). The single best deep-dive; skim chapters.\n- **David Soria Parra (Anthropic) \u2014 \"The Future of MCP\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=v3Fr2JR47KA` (~30 min). Keynote by MCP's co-creator.\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"Claude's Model Context Protocol is here\u2026\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=HyzlYwjoXOQ` (~5 min). Best ADHD-friendly intro.\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"How to make vibe coding not suck\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=PLKrSVuT-Dg` (~5 min).\n- **Theo \u2014 \"MCP is the wrong abstraction\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=bAYZjVAodoo` (~20 min). Critical view \u2014 important so Daniel hears tradeoffs.\n- **Tina Huang \u2014 \"MCP In 26 Minutes\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=kOhLoixrJXo`. Calm, paced.\n- **All About AI \u2014 \"How To Use Anthropic's MCP | Setup Tutorial\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=KiNyvT02HJM`.\n\n**Why MCP over hardcoded/bespoke tool integrations:**\n\n1. **The N\u00d7M \u2192 N+M reduction.** Without a standard, every AI client (Claude Desktop, Cursor, ChatGPT, Gemini) needs custom integrations to every tool (GitHub, Postgres, Slack) \u2014 N\u00d7M total. With MCP, each tool builds *one* server and each client builds *one* MCP layer: N+M.\n2. **\"USB-C port for AI applications\"** \u2014 direct from Anthropic. *\"A universal, open standard\u2026 replacing fragmented integrations with a single protocol.\"*\n3. **Industry adoption proves the standard.** OpenAI adopted MCP **March 2025** (ChatGPT desktop, Agents SDK, Responses API). Google DeepMind: *\"MCP is a good protocol and it's rapidly becoming an open standard for the AI agentic era\"* (Demis Hassabis). Microsoft co-developed an official C# SDK. Dec 2025: Anthropic donated MCP to the Linux Foundation's Agentic AI Foundation with Block and OpenAI as co-founders. ~16,000 MCP servers exist as of mid-2025.\n\n**TV/media analogy:** MCP = XLR / SDI / USB-C for AI. Before XLR, every microphone had a proprietary connector \u2014 you needed a drawer of adapters to plug a Sennheiser into a Sound Devices recorder. XLR made any compliant mic work with any compliant preamp. MCP does the same for AI: any compliant tool (GitHub, Postgres, your filesystem) plugs into any compliant AI (Claude, ChatGPT, Gemini) without a custom adapter.\n\n**Caveats:**\n- MCP is ~18 months old; spec evolved through 2025 (streaming transport, OAuth 2.1, MCP Apps UI extension). Pre-mid-2025 tutorials may show stdio-only transport or pre-OAuth auth. Check dates.\n- Security is the biggest open issue. Local MCP servers can access SSH keys and credentials with \"woefully fragile\" current protections. Treat MCP server installs like browser extensions \u2014 only from trusted sources.\n- Theo's critical \"wrong abstraction\" video is worth watching for balance.\n\n---\n\n### Anthropic SDK for Node.js\n\n**Best free resources:**\n\n- **Official npm page + README** \u2014 `npmjs.com/package/@anthropic-ai/sdk`. Current quickstart with model name (Daniel uses `claude-opus-4-7`).\n- **GitHub repo `anthropics/anthropic-sdk-typescript`** \u2014 `/examples` folder has runnable streaming, tool-use, and structured-output scripts.\n- **Official TS SDK docs** \u2014 `platform.claude.com/docs/en/api/sdks/typescript`. `messages.create`, streaming, retries, error types, timeouts.\n- **Client SDKs overview** \u2014 `platform.claude.com/docs/en/api/client-sdks`. Authoritative source for \"why SDK\": *\"Each SDK provides idiomatic interfaces, type safety, and built-in support for features like streaming, retries, and error handling.\"*\n- **helpers.md \u2014 streaming + Zod structured outputs** \u2014 `github.com/anthropics/anthropic-sdk-typescript/blob/main/helpers.md`. Shows `messages.stream()` events, `messages.parse()` with `zodOutputFormat`. **Bridges Zod \u2194 Anthropic SDK perfectly.**\n- **Anthropic Cookbook** \u2014 `github.com/anthropics/claude-cookbooks`. Tool use, RAG, prompt caching, sub-agents, vision, PDF. Mostly Python, but patterns translate.\n- **API key best practices** \u2014 `support.claude.com/en/articles/9767949-api-key-best-practices-keeping-your-keys-safe-and-secure`. Critical reading.\n\n**YouTube:** Sparse for the Node SDK specifically. Most YouTube covers Python or treats the SDK incidentally. **Lean on docs/cookbook over video for this tool.** Anthropic's official channel `youtube.com/@anthropic-ai` has Code-with-Claude sessions and MCP workshops.\n\n**Why `@anthropic-ai/sdk` over raw `fetch`:**\n\n1. **Typed responses + idiomatic interface.** `message.content` is already typed `ContentBlock[]` with discriminated unions for `text`, `tool_use`, etc. With raw fetch you re-type every response by hand (and Zod it, ironically).\n2. **Streaming helpers + automatic retries.** The SDK ships `messages.stream()` with `.on('text')`, `.on('contentBlock')`, `.on('message')` events and async iteration; `stream.finalMessage()` awaits the whole result. Raw fetch requires parsing SSE byte streams. Retries with exponential backoff on 429/5xx are built in.\n3. **First-class structured outputs with Zod.** `messages.parse({ model, messages, output_config: { format: zodOutputFormat(MySchema) } })` returns `finalMessage.parsed_output` already validated against your Zod schema. **This is the bridge from Zod to the SDK.**\n4. **Officially supported + future-proof.** Anthropic updates model names, beta features, tool runner; raw fetch code rots.\n\n**Why call the Claude API server-side ONLY, never from the browser \u2014 CRITICAL:**\n\n1. **API key exposure = financial loss.** Anything in the browser bundle is readable in DevTools. The `sk-ant-...` prefix is grep-able. *\"Never include your API key in public discussions\u2026 GitHub actively scans public repositories for exposed Claude API keys\u2026 Anthropic automatically deactivates the exposed API key.\"*\n2. **The SDK literally guards against this.** Browser use requires passing `dangerouslyAllowBrowser: true` \u2014 the word \"dangerously\" is in the option name on purpose. *\"In many cases it doesn't make sense to call directly from a browser environment because it could expose the secret API key.\"*\n3. **CORS + rate-limit fairness.** Anthropic API doesn't set permissive CORS for arbitrary origins; even bypassed, every user's browser would share *your* org rate limit, and one abuser throttles everyone.\n4. **Server-side enables guardrails + observability.** Rate-limit per user, log spend, add validation. The canonical pattern: browser talks to your server; your server adds the key and forwards to Anthropic. **The key never leaves the server.**\n\n**TV/media analogies:**\n- SDK vs raw fetch = the manufacturer's official Canon battery + Canon-branded cable vs soldering your own wire from Radio Shack. DIY works until firmware changes or contacts oxidize \u2014 and you lose a shoot day to a connector problem.\n- API key in browser = leaving the studio's corporate Amex taped to the front window, address-side out. Anyone walking past can copy and run up your bill.\n- API key server-side = kept in the production accountant's locked drawer. Crew submits receipts; the accountant pays from the card; the card itself never leaves the office.\n\n**Caveats:**\n- Model names drift fast. Many tutorials show `claude-3-opus-20240229`, `claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022` \u2014 deprecated. Daniel uses `claude-opus-4-7`. Always check `/docs/about-claude/models` before pasting code.\n- Some third-party blogs show **legacy `HUMAN_PROMPT` / `AI_PROMPT` constants** with `completions.create` \u2014 that's the old Completions API. Use `messages.create` for everything new.\n\n**The three-tool stack works like this:** Anthropic SDK sends the request \u2192 MCP is how Claude reaches outward to grab context (files, DBs, APIs) \u2192 Zod validates Claude's structured JSON response and any user input going in (using the SDK's built-in `zodOutputFormat` helper).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Layer 7 \u2014 Toolchain (Node, npm, ESLint)\n\n### Node.js + npm\n\n**Mental model:** Node is a runtime that executes JS outside the browser. `package.json` = project manifest. `node_modules` = dependency cache. `npm install` reads the manifest. `npx` runs a package binary once without global install.\n\n**Resources:**\n- `nodejs.org/en/learn/getting-started/introduction-to-nodejs` \u2014 canonical, short.\n- `docs.npmjs.com/cli/v10/configuring-npm/package-json` \u2014 authoritative; skim.\n- **Fireship's Node.js video** on the Fireship channel; also in the 100-Seconds playlist `youtube.com/playlist?list=PLSId5Ee-5md80GQgzLchOVH9F8YYMyjAh`.\n- **Note:** per `100seconds.dev`, \"npm\" is one of the most-requested but **not-yet-published** Fireship 100-Seconds topics. Substitute the JS + Node videos plus the npm docs.\n- **freeCodeCamp \u2014 \"Getting Started with Node.js\"** (Samer Buna, ~3hr) \u2014 cherry-pick the first 30 min.\n\n**Time:** 25\u201340 min. Stop before Express.\n\n**Why Node:** There is no \"skip Node\" path if using React/Next.js \u2014 npm IS how every JS dependency arrives. Alternatives (Deno, Bun) are worth knowing exist, but Claude Code defaults to Node.\n\n**TV analogies:** Node = the playback machine that runs JS outside the browser (the \"deck\" in the rack). npm = the stock-footage marketplace \u2014 search, install, lock the version. `package.json` = the EDL/project file. `node_modules` = the local media cache (huge \u2014 never archive, always re-pull). `npx` = spinning up a transcoder for a single job.\n\n---\n\n### ESLint\n\n**Mental model:** Static analyzer reading code without running it, flagging rule violations. `npx eslint .` runs it.\n\n**Resources:**\n- `eslint.org/docs/latest/about/` \u2014 one page.\n- `eslint.org/docs/latest/use/core-concepts/` \u2014 skim.\n- **freeCodeCamp \u2014 \"The Essentials of ESLint\"** \u2014 `freecodecamp.org/news/the-essentials-eslint/`. The \"why\" framed beautifully.\n\n**Time:** 15\u201325 min.\n\n**Why ESLint over no linting / Biome / JSHint:** Catches a whole class of bugs at write-time \u2014 undeclared vars, unused imports, accidental `=` vs `==`. For someone directing AI, the linter is your second pair of eyes: AI-generated code that lints clean is provably free of a known list of mistakes. JSHint is dead. Biome is genuinely faster (Rust-based, single tool for lint+format) and is the rising contender, BUT ecosystem support (Next.js, TS, React, Tailwind plugins) is still ESLint-first; Next.js scaffolds with ESLint. Stick with ESLint until you have a reason to switch.\n\n**TV analogy:** The standards-and-practices reviewer / QC pass \u2014 refuses to greenlight code that violates house rules.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Layer 5 \u2014 Python email stdlib\n\n**Mental model:** Three stdlib modules collaborate. `smtplib` = sending (SMTP). `imaplib` = reading (IMAP). `email` = parsing/constructing message bodies.\n\n**cPanel Mail specifics:** IMAP `imap.<his-domain>` port **993 SSL** \u2192 use `imaplib.IMAP4_SSL`. SMTP `mail.<his-domain>` port **465 implicit TLS** \u2192 use `smtplib.SMTP_SSL` (NOT `SMTP` + `starttls()` \u2014 that's port 587).\n\n**Resources:**\n- `docs.python.org/3/library/smtplib.html`\n- `docs.python.org/3/library/imaplib.html`\n- `docs.python.org/3/library/email.examples.html`\n- **Real Python \u2014 Sending Emails With Python** \u2014 `realpython.com/python-send-email/`. **THE tutorial**; covers SMTP_SSL on 465, attachments, HTML.\n- **The Python Code \u2014 reading emails with imaplib** \u2014 `thepythoncode.com/article/reading-emails-in-python`. Full end-to-end with attachments.\n- **Mailtrap smtplib guide** \u2014 `mailtrap.io/blog/python-send-email/`. Production patterns.\n\n**Time:** 45\u201360 min.\n\n**Why stdlib over yagmail / imapclient / exchangelib:**\n\n1. **Zero dependencies.** No supply-chain risk; ships with Python forever.\n2. **Mature.** imaplib has been in stdlib since Python 1.5 (1997). Glacially stable.\n3. **AI tools know it cold.** Every LLM has trained on millions of smtplib examples; Claude Code generates working stdlib code first try.\n4. **The \"ugly API\" objection is real but small.** imaplib's API is RFC-shaped (parse byte responses); it's a 5-line wrapper to clean up, and Real Python's tutorial gives you the wrapper.\n5. **When to reach for third-party:** Exchange/Graph (msgraph-sdk) or high-volume transactional (SendGrid SDK). For plain cPanel IMAP/SMTP, stdlib is correct.\n\n**TV analogies:** `imaplib` = the mailroom inbox clerk (opens the mailbox, hands you each piece). `smtplib` = the mailroom outbound clerk (drops finished letters in the SMTP outgoing tray). `email` = the production assistant assembling the envelope, headers, and attachments.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Layer 9 \u2014 Media pipeline (ffmpeg, fswatch, faster-whisper)\n\n### ffmpeg\n\n**Mental model:** CLI tool that reads media in, transforms it, writes media out. Command shape: `ffmpeg -i input.mp4 [flags] output.mp4`. Daniel needs four operations: extract audio, transcode video, trim/cut, extract a frame.\n\n**Resources:**\n- `ffmpeg.org/documentation.html` \u26a0\ufe0f **NOTORIOUSLY DENSE** \u2014 reference only.\n- `trac.ffmpeg.org/wiki` and the H.264 guide `trac.ffmpeg.org/wiki/Encode/H.264` \u2014 the actually-readable official-adjacent content.\n- **Fireship \u2014 \"FFmpeg in 100 Seconds\"** \u2014 `youtube.com/watch?v=26Mayv5JPz0` \u2705\n- **IMG.LY \u2014 Ultimate Guide to FFmpeg** \u2014 `img.ly/blog/ultimate-guide-to-ffmpeg/`. Long but section-skimmable.\n- **devhints.io/ffmpeg** \u2014 one-page cheatsheet; bookmark this.\n- **steven2358 cheatsheet gist** \u2014 `gist.github.com/steven2358/ba153c642fe2bb1e47485962df07c730`. Most-shared on GitHub.\n\n**Time:** 30\u201345 min. Fireship \u2192 devhints \u2192 bookmark IMG.LY.\n\n**Why ffmpeg despite its complexity:** It is the universal media swiss-army knife. VLC, Handbrake, OBS, DaVinci Resolve's import paths, AWS MediaConvert, every YouTube-style platform \u2014 all wrap ffmpeg or use its libraries. There is literally no general-purpose alternative for arbitrary CLI media manipulation. For Whisper transcription, audio extraction is a one-line ffmpeg call. The pain of the syntax is the price of admission to all programmatic media work. **Good news for Daniel:** he doesn't memorize flags \u2014 Claude Code generates them. He just reads them and verifies they make sense.\n\n**TV analogy:** The universal transcoder \u2014 every NLE, every encoder, every broadcast tool has one inside (Handbrake, OBS, Resolve's import path, AWS MediaConvert). Swiss Army knife with 600 pages of manual.\n\n---\n\n### fswatch\n\n**Mental model:** CLI daemon watching a directory, emitting events on file add/change/remove. Wraps Apple's FSEvents API on macOS. Pipe output into `xargs` or a shell loop. Install: `brew install fswatch`.\n\n**Resources:**\n- `github.com/emcrisostomo/fswatch` \u2014 5.2k stars, MIT, actively maintained.\n- `emcrisostomo.github.io/fswatch/` \u2014 homepage.\n- `emcrisostomo.github.io/fswatch/doc/1.16.0/fswatch.html/Monitors.html` \u2014 explains FSEvents backend.\n\n**Time:** 10\u201315 min \u2014 read README, install, run one example.\n\n**Why fswatch over chokidar / watchdog / raw FSEvents / launchd:**\n- **vs chokidar (Node):** requires a Node app; fswatch is standalone CLI you can wire to any language in one line.\n- **vs Python watchdog:** requires a host Python process.\n- **vs raw FSEvents:** Objective-C/Swift against an Apple framework \u2014 not realistic.\n- **vs `launchd` watch paths:** quirky semantics (one event per batch, no path detail in event).\n- **Bottom line:** fswatch is the right tool when trigger = \"new file landed\" and action = \"run any command.\" It's the broadcast hot-folder pattern, ported to macOS.\n\n**TV analogy:** The hot folder / watch folder in a broadcast ingest workflow \u2014 drop a file, an action fires automatically.\n\n**Typical pattern:** `fswatch -0 /path/to/dropzone | xargs -0 -n 1 -I {} python process.py {}` \u2014 run as a launchd agent to survive reboot.\n\n---\n\n### faster-whisper (brief reminder)\n\nPer official README: *\"This implementation is up to 4 times faster than openai/whisper for the same accuracy while using less memory.\"* Reimplementation on top of **CTranslate2** with INT8/FP16 quantization, fused attention kernels, SIMD CPU code. Same model weights, same accuracy \u2014 better execution. On Apple Silicon CPU with INT8, a 13-min clip transcribes in ~1\u20132 min vs vanilla whisper's 4\u20138 min. For a producer cranking through interview audio, that's the difference between \"useful\" and \"let me get coffee.\"\n\n---\n\n## 8. Cross-cutting \"why\" \u2014 guardrails\n\n### Why squash merges\n\nGitHub's docs: *\"If you squash these commits into one commit when merging to the default branch, the changes are consolidated, leading to a clear Git history.\"* Each feature \u2192 single atomic commit on `main` \u2192 one-click revert. Critical for AI-directed dev: when Claude Code goes down a wrong path for an hour, that whole exploratory branch collapses to a single commit (or gets discarded). `main` reads like a release changelog, not a stream-of-consciousness journal.\n\n**TV analogy:** Delivering a single locked master cut to the client, not the 47 intermediate edit versions. The 47 versions stay in your local project; only the master shows up in the master library.\n\n### Why all automation must go through CLOUD APIs \u2014 never touch production hardware/NAS/VPN directly\n\nThis is an **architectural guardrail**, not a tool preference. Four overlapping principles:\n\n1. **Separation of concerns.** The automation layer (AI scripts, Supabase, n8n) is *new, experimental, changes daily*. The on-air chain (broadcast switcher, ProPresenter, NAS, VPN) is *production, stable, changes monthly with rehearsal*. Mixing them means a syntax error takes a service off-air.\n\n2. **Blast radius.** A bad cloud API call returns a 4xx \u2014 you fix it. A bad command to the NAS or switcher \u2192 corrupted asset, lost edit, dropped feed, dead air. Cloud APIs have rate-limiting, auth, validation, audit logs as a moat between intent and damage. Direct hardware access has none.\n\n3. **The \"David Rule.\"** David hosts on-air. He's personally exposed when the show breaks. Any command from Daniel's automation that lands on David's live chain is a command for which David takes the public hit. The ethical posture: automation owns its own data plane, period. If you need to influence production, you publish to a queue/database; production *pulls from* the queue on its own schedule, with its own validation.\n\n4. **Unrecoverable live failures.** A web app outage rolls back in 30 seconds. A live broadcast outage cannot. Treat the broadcast switcher, ProPresenter, and the NAS as if they live behind glass \u2014 read-only via API, never touched directly by automation.\n\nThis isn't \"security best practice\" abstraction \u2014 it's **safety-of-life-of-broadcast**. Every architecture decision (Supabase as the bus, webhooks from cloud, production polls cloud) follows from it.\n\n**TV analogy:** The **air gap between automation and the live broadcast chain**. You never let the automation rig touch the on-air router, switcher, or NAS directly. Automation publishes to a cloud bus; production *pulls* from the bus.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Revised module sequence (the key recommendation)\n\n### Critical evaluation of the stated priority order\n\nApplying scaffolding (Vygotsky), spiral curriculum (Bruner), concreteness-fading (Goldstone & Sakamoto), and backward-design (Wiggins & McTighe):\n\n| His order | Verdict | Reason |\n|---|---|---|\n| 1. TypeScript | **Move later** | TS on day 1 for a non-coder with no JS mental model is pure abstraction without anything to type-check. Concreteness-fading says start concrete. |\n| 2. React/Next.js | **Move later** | Can't run React without Node + npm. Can't sensibly discuss components without \"what is client vs server.\" |\n| 3. SQL/Postgres/RLS | **Split** | SQL basics early as vivid mental model (\"a spreadsheet you query\"). RLS belongs much later, with Supabase. |\n| 4. Supabase | **Move later** | Supabase IS a REST API. Doing Supabase before REST is teaching the abstraction before the thing it abstracts. |\n| 5. REST/fetch | **Move earlier** | Foundational mental model for everything else (Supabase, MCP, third-party APIs). |\n| 6. Zod | **Keep late** | Correct \u2014 Zod only makes sense after feeling the pain of unvalidated JSON. |\n| 7. MCP | **Keep late** | Correct \u2014 needs REST first. |\n| 8. Python | **Move earlier** | He'll write more Python automation than React. |\n| 9. Git/GitHub | **Move way earlier** | **Single biggest mistake.** Git is the safety net. He needs `init`, `commit`, `revert` BEFORE Claude Code touches a single file. |\n| 10. ffmpeg+Whisper | **Keep late, tie to project** | Correct, but motivate by an actual transcription project. |\n\n### Direct answers to the sequencing questions\n\n- **Git earlier?** YES, Module 1. Non-negotiable. The seatbelt before the car moves.\n- **REST before Supabase?** YES. Supabase is \"Postgres with auto-generated REST endpoints + row-level auth.\" Without REST mental model, every Supabase call is magic.\n- **Foundational models before React?** YES, Module 0. Client/server/database/request/response are 4 concepts that must precede everything.\n- **Node/npm before React?** YES. React doesn't run without them.\n- **Split TypeScript?** YES. TS-lite (annotate vars, params, basic interfaces) early; TS-deep (generics, `z.infer`) only when Zod demands it.\n- **Cloud-API guardrail early?** YES, Module 0. Pre-load as mental model before any tool \u2014 it determines the architecture of everything else.\n\n### Proposed CORE PATH (~7 hours, 9 modules)\n\n**Module 0 \u2014 Mental Models & Guardrails** *(45 min, no prereqs)*\nClient vs server. What a database actually is. Request/response cycle. What an API is. What JSON is. **The cloud-API-only rule as architectural law.** JavaScript vs Python (when to use which). What \"running code\" means (browser, Node, Python interpreter).\n*Rationale:* Pre-loads vocabulary so every later module has hooks to attach to. The cloud-only guardrail is established BEFORE any tool \u2014 so every later choice is filtered through it.\n*Resources:* MDN HTTP overview, Fireship \"JavaScript in 100 Seconds\" (`youtube.com/watch?v=DHjqpvDnNGE`), one custom diagram of \"automation layer \u2194 cloud APIs \u2194 production chain\" with the David Rule called out.\n\n**Module 1 \u2014 Git/GitHub as Safety Net** *(45 min)*\n`git init`, `status`, `add`, `commit -m`, `log`, `diff`. Then `restore` and `revert` (undo buttons). GitHub: create repo, push, branch, PR. **Squash merge as default.** SSH key setup. `.gitignore`.\n*Rationale:* Before AI touches code, he needs the safety net. Every subsequent module assumes everything happens inside a git repo. Spiral: branching reinforced every later module.\n*Resources:* GitHub Skills `skills.github.com` (free, interactive), Fireship \"Git in 100 Seconds\" (`youtube.com/watch?v=hwP7WQkmECE`), `docs.github.com/articles/about-pull-request-merges`.\n\n**Module 2 \u2014 Terminal, Node, npm** *(45 min)*\nTerminal basics (`cd`, `ls`, `pwd`). Install Node via official installer or `brew`. `node -v`, `npm -v`. What `package.json` is (manifest). What `node_modules` is (cache \u2014 never commit; that's why `.gitignore` was Module 1). `npm install <pkg>` vs `-D`. `npx <pkg>` = run-once. `npm run <script>`.\n*Rationale:* The substrate everything JS sits on. He's learning Node not to write Node but so he can read what Claude Code does without being mystified by \"node_modules\" errors.\n\n**Module 3 \u2014 HTTP, REST & fetch** *(45 min)*\nGET/POST/PUT/DELETE. Status codes. Headers (`Authorization`, `Content-Type`). Request bodies. `curl` from terminal. `fetch()` from browser console. What \"REST\" means (resources at URLs).\n*Rationale:* Bedrock model for Supabase, MCP, every third-party integration. Concreteness: he hits real APIs with curl before writing code. **Spiral checkpoint:** revisits Module 0's \"request/response\" with a concrete curl command.\n\n**Module 4 \u2014 SQL & Postgres (concrete first)** *(60 min)*\nTables, rows, columns, primary/foreign keys. `SELECT`, `WHERE`, `INSERT`, `UPDATE`, `DELETE`, `JOIN`. Why Postgres vs SQLite vs MySQL. Run queries against real Postgres in Supabase's SQL editor.\n*Rationale:* Database is the most concrete metaphor (a spreadsheet with rules). Before TypeScript and React because schema is upstream \u2014 \"data shapes the app.\" RLS deferred to Module 7 \u2014 too abstract without first feeling \"anyone can read anything.\"\n*Resources:* SQLBolt `sqlbolt.com` (free interactive ~1hr, gold standard), Supabase SQL beginners doc.\n\n**Module 5 \u2014 Python Basics for Automation** *(60 min)*\nInstall Python 3.12+. `python3` REPL. Variables, lists, dicts, functions, if/for. `pip install` + **virtual environments**. File I/O. `requests`. Stdlib: `os`, `pathlib`, `json`, `subprocess`. Brief preview of `imaplib`/`smtplib` (deep-dive in Module 9).\n*Rationale:* Python is where his automation glue lives. Gentler first language than TypeScript. Moved up because he'll write more Python than JS day-to-day.\n*Resources:* \"Python for Everybody\" `py4e.com` (free), Real Python.\n\n**Module 6 \u2014 TypeScript Basics (TS-lite)** *(45 min)*\nWhy types (catch bugs before runtime, real autocomplete). Annotations: `string`, `number`, `boolean`, arrays, objects. `interface` and `type`. Optional fields. Function signatures. **Skip** generics, conditional types, utility types, `infer`.\n*Rationale:* Just enough to read Next.js code Claude writes. Advanced TS returns in Module 10 with Zod. **Spiral:** the JSON from Module 3's fetch responses now has a shape \u2014 that shape is a TypeScript interface.\n*Resources:* TS Handbook \"Everyday Types,\" Fireship \"TypeScript in 100 Seconds\" (`youtube.com/watch?v=zQnBQ4tB3ZA`).\n\n**Module 7 \u2014 Supabase + RLS (spiral on SQL)** *(75 min)*\nCreate a Supabase project. Schema in SQL editor. **Supabase IS a REST API** (`/rest/v1/` auto-generated). The JS client `@supabase/supabase-js`. Auth basics. Then **RLS**: write policies in SQL, enable on every table, `anon` vs `authenticated`, `auth.uid()`. The \"RLS off = your DB is public\" rule.\n*Rationale:* Concreteness-fading at its peak \u2014 already knows SQL (M4) and REST (M3); Supabase = those two stapled together. **Spiral:** SQL revisited as policy language; REST revisited with auto-generated endpoints.\n*Resources:* Supabase docs, Supabase RLS guide, Supabase YouTube Crash Course.\n\n**Module 8 \u2014 React + Next.js App Router** *(90 min)*\nComponents, props, `useState`, `useEffect`. JSX. Next.js App Router file routing: `app/page.tsx`, `app/api/route.ts`. **Server Components vs Client Components** (the `\"use client\"` directive). Calling Supabase from a server component. Deploying to Vercel.\n*Rationale:* Last in core path on purpose. React only makes sense when there's something to render (data from Supabase via REST, typed by TS, fetched in Node-land). **Spiral checkpoints:** TypeScript, Node, REST, Supabase ALL reinforced in a working app.\n*Resources:* Official Next.js Learn (`nextjs.org/learn`), Fireship \"Next.js in 100 Seconds\" + \"React in 100 Seconds.\"\n\n**END OF CORE PATH \u2014 ~7 hours total.**\n\n### OPTIONAL DEEPER DIVES\n\n**Module 9 \u2014 Python Email Automation (imaplib + smtplib + email)** *(60 min)*\n`imaplib.IMAP4_SSL(host, 993)` for cPanel. `smtplib.SMTP_SSL(host, 465)`. `email.message.EmailMessage`. Parsing inbound MIME. Sending with attachments. **Architectural framing:** the mail script runs *in cloud* (VPS, GitHub Action, Supabase Edge Function), writes to Supabase; production reads from Supabase. Script never touches on-air infrastructure.\n\n**Module 10 \u2014 Zod + TypeScript-Deep** *(45 min)*\nZod schemas as runtime validators of untrusted JSON (every API response from outside). `z.infer<typeof Schema>` to derive TS type \u2014 single source of truth. Use Zod at every API boundary: `fetch().then(r => r.json()).then(Schema.parse)`. **Spiral:** TypeScript revisited \u2014 now you need `infer`, generics, utility types.\n\n**Module 11 \u2014 MCP (Model Context Protocol)** *(45 min)*\nMCP = standardized protocol for LLMs to call tools/resources. \"REST for AI.\" Connect Claude Desktop or Claude Code to an MCP server. Use off-the-shelf servers (filesystem, Postgres, Supabase). When to write your own.\n\n**Module 12 \u2014 ESLint + Code Quality Gates** *(30 min)*\n`npm install -D eslint`. `npx eslint --init`. `npx eslint .`. VS Code fix-on-save. Integrating with Next.js scaffolded config. Why it matters specifically for AI-directed work: deterministic check on AI output.\n\n**Module 13 \u2014 ffmpeg + Whisper Pipeline** *(75 min)*\nInstall ffmpeg via brew. Four operations: extract audio (`ffmpeg -i in.mp4 -vn -acodec pcm_s16le -ar 16000 -ac 1 out.wav`), transcode, trim, thumbnail. Then `pip install faster-whisper`. Transcribe extracted audio. Wire together with a Python script.\n\n**Module 14 \u2014 fswatch + Hot-Folder Automation** *(20 min)*\n`brew install fswatch`. `fswatch -0 /path/to/dropzone | xargs -0 -n 1 -I {} python process.py {}`. Run as launchd agent.\n\n### Spiral curriculum map\n\n| Topic introduced in | Revisited in | What gets deepened |\n|---|---|---|\n| Git (M1) | Every later module | branching, squash merges, .gitignore for node_modules and .venv |\n| Client/server (M0) | M3 (HTTP), M7 (Supabase), M8 (Server vs Client Components) | \"where does this code run?\" gets sharper |\n| REST (M3) | M7 (Supabase IS REST), M11 (MCP is REST-shaped), M10 (Zod validates REST responses) | abstract \u2192 concrete \u2192 typed |\n| SQL (M4) | M7 (Supabase queries + RLS policies in SQL) | SQL as policy language |\n| TypeScript-lite (M6) | M8 (React props), M10 (z.infer + generics) | basic types \u2192 derived types |\n| Python (M5) | M9 (imaplib/smtplib), M13 (Whisper orchestration) | scripting \u2192 integration |\n| Cloud-API-only rule (M0) | M9, M13, M14 | recurs every time touching hardware is tempting |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Master TV/media analogy table\n\n| Concept | Broadcast / NLE analogy |\n|---|---|\n| Node.js | The playback machine that runs JS outside the browser \u2014 the \"deck\" in the rack |\n| npm | The stock-footage marketplace \u2014 search, install, lock the version in `package.json` |\n| `package.json` | The EDL / project file \u2014 manifest of every external clip with version numbers |\n| `node_modules` | The local media cache. Huge. Never archive (`.gitignore` it). Re-pull anytime |\n| `npx` | Spinning up a transcoder for a single job without installing it permanently |\n| ESLint | The standards-and-practices reviewer / QC pass \u2014 refuses to greenlight code violating house rules |\n| TypeScript | The script supervisor \u2014 checks the script matches what talent is about to say, before the take |\n| Zod | The QC engineer at ingest \u2014 every external file validated against spec before it hits the SAN |\n| ffmpeg | The universal transcoder \u2014 every NLE/encoder/broadcast tool has one inside |\n| fswatch | The hot folder / watch folder \u2014 drop a file, action fires automatically |\n| `imaplib` | The mailroom inbox clerk \u2014 opens the IMAP mailbox, hands you each piece |\n| `smtplib` | The mailroom outbound clerk \u2014 drops finished letters in the SMTP tray |\n| Git | Versioned project saves \u2014 every commit is a save-state |\n| Squash merge | Delivering a single locked master cut, not the 47 intermediate edit versions |\n| Branch | A scratch project on a duplicate timeline \u2014 experiment without touching the master |\n| GitHub PR | The screening / approval session before the master goes into the archive |\n| REST API | The intercom / tally protocol between rooms \u2014 standardized requests, standardized responses |\n| PostgreSQL | The media archive / MAM system (Avid Interplay, Iconik) \u2014 clips in bins with structured metadata |\n| Supabase | Rented turnkey production facility \u2014 stages, edit bays, vault, security desk, runners, late-night control room \u2014 all under one roof |\n| Row-Level Security | Keycard rules on the asset database \u2014 even a stolen keycard can't see other people's content |\n| Magic-link auth | Single-use stage passes emailed to talent |\n| SECURITY DEFINER function | The executive producer briefly stamping a request with director-level authority for one audited approval |\n| React | The on-air graphics engine \u2014 declarative templates re-rendering when data changes |\n| React component | A reusable lower-thirds template instanced per segment |\n| Next.js | A fully-equipped studio \u2014 cameras, lights, audio board, teleprompter, uplink, edit bay |\n| Plain React (Vite) | An empty soundstage \u2014 bring your own gear |\n| App Router vs Pages Router | Newer IP/SDI broadcast workflow vs older tape-based \u2014 both ship a show; new productions choose the new one |\n| Server Component | Pre-rendered title card / character generator pre-roll \u2014 baked, ready, shipped |\n| Client Component | Live graphics overlay reacting to user input on air |\n| Server Action | A button on the production switcher that fires a server-side macro |\n| Tailwind | The show's brand kit / style guide \u2014 fixed palette, type scale, spacing |\n| Plain CSS | Re-mixing the brand colors on every shot |\n| shadcn/ui | Unlocked b-roll footage you license outright and re-edit \u2014 you own the masters |\n| MUI / Chakra / Ant | A stock-music subscription \u2014 you can fade volume but can't change the melody |\n| Radix | A professional audio console with no faceplate \u2014 every fader is broadcast-spec, no styling |\n| Vercel | The broadcast distribution network \u2014 CDN edge (affiliates), bandwidth, SSL, transmission |\n| Preview deployment | Dailies / rough-cut screening links \u2014 every push is a screener URL |\n| Edge runtime | Local affiliate stations rebroadcasting from the closest tower |\n| Serverless function | Freelance crew per shoot \u2014 only pay when filming; cold start = ramp-up time; no memory of yesterday |\n| Long-running server | Full-time staff on payroll 24/7 \u2014 instantly responsive, remembers everything, pay regardless |\n| VPS | Owning your own studio + transmitter tower \u2014 maximum control, FCC paperwork is yours |\n| Anthropic SDK | The manufacturer's official Canon cable \u2014 works, gets firmware-matched updates |\n| Raw `fetch` to API | Soldering your own wire from Radio Shack \u2014 works until firmware changes or contacts oxidize |\n| API key in browser | Studio's corporate Amex taped to the front window, address-side out |\n| API key server-side | Card in the production accountant's locked drawer \u2014 crew submits receipts, accountant pays |\n| MCP | XLR / SDI / USB-C for AI \u2014 any compliant tool plugs into any compliant AI without custom adapters |\n| Python | The shop's swiss-army utility scripting language \u2014 the gaffer-tape of automation |\n| Whisper / faster-whisper | The automated transcriber on staff \u2014 feeds audio in, gets timecoded text out. faster-whisper = same person after a productivity course (4\u00d7 faster, same accuracy) |\n| Cloud-API-only rule | The **air gap between automation and the live broadcast chain** \u2014 automation publishes to a cloud bus; production *pulls* from the bus on its own schedule. The David Rule: the host is exposed when it breaks, so the architecture protects the host. |\n\n---\n\n## 11. Legacy stack footnote\n\nn8n (workflow orchestration), Playwright (browser automation), and standalone CLI scripts (youtubeuploader, basic-ftp, dropbox-sdk-js) are **superseded** by the Next.js / Supabase / Vercel approach. Keep as a one-line label in the curriculum (\"Legacy \u2014 not in current build\") and do not allocate lesson time. If a script in `gsr-legacy/` ever needs a one-off rerun, the relevant tool is named on the script \u2014 that's enough.\n\n---\n\n## 12. Bottom-line takeaways for the lesson author\n\n1. **Re-sequence aggressively.** Daniel's stated order is a priority list, not a learning sequence. Git first, REST before Supabase, foundations before React, Python before TypeScript-deep.\n2. **Build every Next.js lesson around App Router corrections.** Add a fixed \"Tell Claude\" prompt block in every Next.js lesson reminding him to specify App Router, no `pages/`, no `getServerSideProps`.\n3. **Build every Supabase lesson around `@supabase/ssr`.** Aggressively flag and avoid `@supabase/auth-helpers-nextjs` content. Jon Meyers's \"UPDATED\" video (`watch?v=v6UvgfSIjQ0`) is the single most important video in this category.\n4. **Zod's purpose only clicks after the pain.** Don't teach Zod before he's seen an unvalidated JSON response break a Next.js page.\n5. **The cloud-API-only rule belongs in Module 0**, framed as architectural law (the David Rule) \u2014 not buried as a footnote in a security lesson.\n6. **Fireship \"100 Seconds\" videos are perfect ADHD opening hooks** for almost every module. Confirmed available: React, Next.js, Tailwind, PostgreSQL, Supabase, Git, TypeScript, JavaScript, ffmpeg, MCP. Confirmed *not* available: npm, Zod, shadcn, Vercel, Anthropic SDK. Substitute the official docs for those slots.\n7. **For tools without strong free video content (Anthropic SDK, Radix, fswatch),** lean on official docs + the GitHub `/examples` folders.\n8. **The three-AI-tools form a working stack:** Anthropic SDK sends the request \u2192 MCP fetches outside context \u2192 Zod validates the response. Use the SDK's `zodOutputFormat` helper as the literal code bridge \u2014 and teach it in that order.",
